AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Cadbury: nuts vs peanuts
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: cadbury-nuts-vs-peanuts
CATEGORY: Food and Drink
CATEGORY: Me

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/11/cadbury-nuts-vs-peanuts.html 
DATE: 11/28/2009 12:30:30 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>I like a bit of chocolate, but my peanut allergy means I have to read the labels very carefully. One major annoyance is when I find the text &quot;may contain nuts&quot; or similar. The dilemma I face is that peanuts are not technically nuts - they are a legume, more like actual peas than nuts. <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peanut" target="_blank">Honest, it&#39;s true</a>. So, when I read &quot;may contain nuts&quot; does the manufacturer appreciate this distinction (in which case I am safe) or are they including peanuts as nuts, as the common man on the street would most likely expect (in which case I am not safe)?</p><p>I asked Cadbury what their position on this is. Here&#39;s what I sent them:</p><p><em><span style="color: #7f007f; "><span style="color: #3b5738; ">As anyone in your industry likely knows, peanuts are not technically nuts - they are a legume. Can you clarify whether Cadbury labelling (e.g. on Cadbury Clusters) that says &quot;May contain nuts&quot; &#0160;includes peanuts in its remit or not? On a technicality I would think not and that I (as a peanut allergy sufferer) could eat the product with impunity. However it might be that you interpret &quot;nuts&quot; to include peanuts. Some companies specifically say &quot;tree nuts&quot; to be clear when they means nuts but not peanuts. I&#39;m keen to understand Cadbury&#39;s position here so I know what&#39;s safe to eat and what&#39;s not. Thanks in advance. Either way, it would be helpful to all nut and peanut allergy sufferers if the labelling could be made unambiguous and I&#39;d appreciate a comment on that more generally.</span></span></em></p><p><font color="#7F007F"><span style="color: #111111; ">The response from Cadbury (over a month later, after me chasing them):</span></font></p><p><font color="#7F007F"><span style="color: #111111; "></span><em>Thanks for your email</em></font></p><p><font color="#7F007F"><em>Our Technical area advise&#0160;Cadbury labels Nuts when referring to Tree nuts. We would label Peanuts&#0160;separately as they are not a Tree nut as correctly pointed out.</em></font></p><p><font color="#7F007F"><span style="color: #111111; ">So, there&#39;s your answer, for Cadbury at least. It&#39;s a shame they didn&#39;t see fit to comment on perhaps using &quot;tree nuts&quot; in their labelling in order to be unambiguous.</span></font></p>

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Kitchen shelves
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: kitchen-shelves
CATEGORY: Books
CATEGORY: Design
CATEGORY: DIY
CATEGORY: Food and Drink
CATEGORY: Me

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/11/kitchen-shelves.html 
DATE: 11/19/2009 11:06:37 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>Our kitchen had one patch of bare wall but nowhere to put cookbooks other than in a pile on a worktop. A perfect opportunity for some bookshelves! I planned a custom construction made from pine, comprising two uprights resting on the floor with four cross pieces (for three shelves and a top) with the whole thing screwed to the wall for rock solidness.</p>

<p><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e01588834012875ba0616970c-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="float: right; padding-left:15px; padding-bottom: 10px;"><img alt="KitchenShelves" class="asset asset-image at-xid-6a00e5550e01588834012875ba0616970c " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e01588834012875ba0616970c-200wi" style="width: 200px; margin: 0px 0px 5px 5px;" /></a></p>

<p>I originally expected to use 18mm thick sawn pine timber, but in B&amp;Q it was clear that these were actually quite warped end to end - the top of a 2.4m plank was about 30 degrees twisted compared to the bottom so that it would have messed up the result something chronic. Instead I bought pine &quot;furniture board&quot; which is engineered from multiple pieces of pine glued together (edge to edge, not ply) which gives a much less lively result with hardly any warp whilst looking quite attractive. It&#39;s quite a lot more expensive mind you, and having waited 30 minutes for the timber cutting service to re-open after lunch I was told my 20cm wide boards were not suitable for the machine. At 2.4m long they weren&#39;t going to fit in the car so a hasty re-planning was required, resulting in the purchase of a number of smaller 25cm wide pre-cut pieces. I&#39;m glad I went for that width actually as many of the books are 22cm and there&#39;s room to accommodate that depth from the wall even though I was worried there wouldn&#39;t be.</p>

<p>I had been keen to get all the lengths cut in store for a perfectly square, straight cut with identical lengths for all the shelves. I don&#39;t have a table saw so I was going to struggle to do this easily myself, but I was forced to saw the boards down to the right length with a hand saw. It was tough to get a good result here and to get them all the exact same length, but the flex in the uprights accommodated the differences. I simply put two number 8 screws into the end of each shelf to hold it in place, with carefully drilled countersunk screw holes, and that seems to have done the job. The countersink bit I bought recently is a godsend - it really makes the results look so much more professional.</p>

<p>A couple of simple metal angle brackets off the peg from B&amp;Q allowed me to screw the whole ensemble firmly to the wall and it really is very rigid. Also note in the picture (click for bigger version) the 45 degree cut off on the tops of the side pieces and the cut-outs at the bottom to allow it to sit flush against the wall above the skirting.</p>

<p>Overall I&#39;m extremely pleased with the result apart from one thing. I slightly lost track of of the height of my biggest books between start and end of the project, the result being that they don&#39;t quite fit on the shelves by a few millimetres. I&#39;m kicking myself about this, but I&#39;m a novice and I&#39;ll learn from these mistakes.</p>

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: RVM and NetBeans
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: rvm-and-netbeans
CATEGORY: Mac
CATEGORY: Programming
CATEGORY: Ruby
CATEGORY: Web/Tech

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/10/rvm-and-netbeans.html 
DATE: 10/25/2009 10:06:30 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>I&#39;ve been having a lot of trouble with my Ruby 1.9.1 install on Mac OS X. Mostly it works fine, but I struggle when installing gems that require native extensions. I think this is because the way my install was built causes linkage problems, perhaps due to 32 vs 64 bit issues, or due to linkage with other libraries. I&#39;m not entirely sure what&#39;s causing the problems, but recently I decided enough was enough and tried out <a href="http://rvm.beginrescueend.com/" target="_blank">rvm</a>&#0160;since I&#39;ve heard a lot of good things about it. I got the impression that by compiling from my own source I was stubbornly making a lot of my own trouble.</p>

<p>Rvm is trivial to install: it&#39;s a gem that installs some of its own executables. I did hack my PATH first, to remove&#0160;/usr/local/bin (where my custom Ruby lived) so that I&#39;d be using the stock Mac OS X Ruby for the rvm install.</p>

<p></p>

<p>&gt; sudo gem install rvm<br />&gt; rvm-install</p>

<p></p>

<p>Note that rvm-install added the following to the end of ~/.bash_profile automatically, so I could ignore the instruction it gave me about adding it myself:</p>

<p><span style="font-family: Courier;">if [ -s ~/.rvm/scripts/rvm ] ; then source ~/.rvm/scripts/rvm ; fi</span></p>

<p>I then used rvm to install a fresh version of Ruby 1.9.1:
&gt;&gt; rvm install 1.9.1</p>

<p>Actually that failed with an error about libsqlite3.dylib being the wrong architecture - perhaps another hangover from my old manual installs, or a problem I&#39;m going to have to solve sometime in the future! For now I moved the old version of that file and tried again:</p>
<p>&gt; sudo mv /usr/local/lib/libsqlite3.dylib /usr/local/lib/libsqlite3.dylibOLD<br />&gt; rvm install 1.9.1</p><p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica"></p>

<p>And that left me with a decent ruby 1.9.1 install. Which brought me back to one of the things that I was originally frustrated by: getting NetBeans Ruby debugging working with the fast debugger. With my old install the ruby-debug-ide gem would not install, but I&#39;m pleased to report that it does with this new setup.</p>
<p>However getting NetBeans to actually use my new rvm ruby required a bit of a trick. The Ruby Platform management GUI in NetBeans doesn&#39;t show you hidden folders in its file picker, so you can&#39;t navigate to the ~/.rvm/ruby-1.9.1-p243/bin/ruby file that it wants. The trick is to create a non-hidden symlink, so you can then find it from NetBeans (and it&#39;s also handy to get at your rvm files from Finder):</p>

<p>&gt; ln -s ~/.rvm ~/rvm</p>

<p>One word of warning: once you&#39;re using an RVM Ruby install, <strong>do not use sudo for gem installs</strong>, as the gems (and every part of rvm) live in ~/.rvm so sudo is not required. In fact using sudo will knacker your gems quite badly as it gets its PATH wrong and its permissions and you end up deleting a bunch of stuff to get back to a known good state. I learnt this the hard way!</p>

<p></p>

<p></p>

<p></p>
-----

It looks like the "solution" for this in 10.6 is currently:

sudo ln -s /Developer/SDKs/MacOSX10.6.sdk/usr/lib/libsqlite3.0.dylib /usr/local/lib/libsqlite3.dylib

(With attribution to the source at <a href="http://twitter.com/eoinbrazil/status/6482799633)">http://twitter.com/eoinbrazil/status/6482799633)</a>

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Ten Quid Cupboard
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: 0
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: ten-quid-cupboard
CATEGORY: Me

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/10/ten-quid-cupboard.html 
DATE: 10/18/2009 10:05:11 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>We had a particular space to fill next to the sofa in our new house, and wanted a low sideboard to house our extensive and exotic booze collection, which up until now has been gathering dust on the floor in a corner. However the space is only 82cm wide and most pieces of suitable furniture we've seen are at least a metre wide, and often too tall compared to the 69cm high sofa.</p>

<p>We set off on Saturday with a medium length list of places to try in our grim search for just the right solution, but we struck lucky at our first stop: <a href="http://www.emmaus.org.uk/" target="_blank">Emmaus</a> in St Albans. This place is basically a second hand furniture shop with fairly rapid turnover, but it's more than just that, being run as a community to get homeless people back on their feet. We've been a couple of times before and not found anything for us, but this time round for <strong>just £10</strong> we came away with an 84 cm wide cupboard that sits just perfectly in our previously empty space.</p>

<p><p style="text-align: center;"><a style="display: inline;" href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a5f2c692970b-pi"><img  class="asset asset-image at-xid-6a00e5550e015888340120a5f2c692970b " alt="EmmausCupboard" title="EmmausCupboard" src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a5f2c692970b-800wi" border="0" /></a>&nbsp;</p></p>

<p>Isn't that 2cm too wide you may ask? Yes, so I had to remove the beading at the edge of the laminate floor to make enough room for a very snug fit.</p>

<p>Our collection of exotic and nauseous booze will now reside within, perhaps lying undisturbed for decades until young teenagers nick it late at night. And so the cycle repeats.</p>

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: MacRuby 0.5 beta 1 Released
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: macruby-05-beta-1-released
CATEGORY: Mac
CATEGORY: Programming
CATEGORY: Ruby
CATEGORY: Web/Tech

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/10/macruby-05-beta-1-released.html 
DATE: 10/11/2009 10:39:31 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>I was very excited to see <a href="http://www.macruby.org/blog/2009/10/07/macruby05b1.html" target="_blank">MacRuby 0.5 beta 1</a> had been announced, complete with ahead of time compilation via LLVM. It has been long while since the previous update on the MacRuby blog in March, but clearly a lot of work has been taking place. At the moment this beta shows the promise of things to come but isn&#39;t yet fit for much more than anticipatory experimentation. If you want to try the macrubyc compiler, <a href="http://antoniocangiano.com/2009/10/08/getting-macrubys-compiler-to-work/" target="_blank">Antonio Cangiano&#39;s blog post on the topic</a> is a must-read.</p><p>The MacRuby notes suggest that compiled ahead of time or not, it uses LLVM for a big speed win, but my own quick experiment showed the macruby interpreter to be about 3 times slower than the standard MRI Ruby 1.9.1. This was with a single small benchmark app only though, just to prove things were working, so I can&#39;t draw conclusions. I can&#39;t pretend I wasn&#39;t a little disappointed not to see MRI blown out of the water though, even though I know it&#39;s unscientific and wrong of me!</p><p>I couldn&#39;t get a fully compiled version to produce any output, though it appeared to run without barfing, so I couldn&#39;t tell if it was really working or not. It was notable that the compiled binary was nearly 15MB so there must be a lot of statically linked code being included to swell my couple of KB of Ruby code so much. I&#39;m hopeful that this can be improved in the future in order to support my dream of iPhone apps being written with Ruby hooking into Cocoa. In fact more than a dream - I&#39;m hopeful and optimistic that in the long-run Apple will make Ruby a heavily promoted first class citizen for Mac and iPhone development, sitting on top of Objective-C but hiding it for the most part. The whole world has moved on from primitive C-based languages to higher levels of abstraction and I think Apple really needs a successor to Objective-C within the next 5 years. Is MacRuby it?</p>
-----

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: New Shed Roof
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: new-shed-roof
CATEGORY: DIY

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/10/new-shed-roof.html 
DATE: 10/05/2009 09:46:51 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>One of the sheds I inherited when I moved into the new house had a bit of a dodgy roof, with the felt rather ragged and exposing the wood around the edges. In the recent strong winds half of the felt actually peeled back and flopped to one side like a bad combover, so with lots of rain forecast for this week I figured I had to act swiftly to keep things dry.</p>

<p>According to their website Homebase don&#39;t actually sell roof felt (though they do sell the nails) so it was Wickes that sorted me out: £11 for an 8 metre roll of felt and a couple of quid more for a ridiculous quantity of &#39;galvanised 13mm extra large head clout nails&#39;. A bargain surely.</p>

<p></p><p style="text-align: center;"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a616e6e4970c-pi" style="display: inline;"><img alt="ShedRoof1" border="0" class="asset asset-image at-xid-6a00e5550e015888340120a616e6e4970c " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a616e6e4970c-800wi" title="ShedRoof1" /></a>&#0160;</p> <p></p>

<p>It turned out to be surprisingly straightforward to get the old felt off and the new stuff on, even with no access to the side and rear aspects. I was done within just a couple of hours. I had to do most of the work from perching on the roof itself, which was only just robust enough to support me. The special nails are a joy to work with: push them into the felt with a thumb and they stand up on their own, then two whacks with a hammer and they&#39;re in. Very satisfying.</p><p><p style="text-align: center;"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a616e76d970c-pi" style="display: inline;"><img alt="ShedRoof2" border="0" class="asset asset-image at-xid-6a00e5550e015888340120a616e76d970c " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a616e76d970c-800wi" title="ShedRoof2" /></a>&#0160;</p></p><p>The only thing that went wrong was a misdirected hammer blow when leant over the rear, fighting amongst tree branches, which ripped a hole in the felt. I was nearly done at this point so wasn&#39;t keen to rip it all off and start again, but luckily the tarry felt could be pudged back together with a thumb in such a way that it&#39;s probably sufficiently waterproof. I&#39;ll have to keep an eye on that. It was also tough not to damage the felt when climbing all over it, which explains the scuff marks in the photo below.</p><p style="text-align: center;"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a616e7e1970c-pi" style="display: inline;"><img alt="ShedRoof3" border="0" class="asset asset-image at-xid-6a00e5550e015888340120a616e7e1970c " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a616e7e1970c-800wi" title="ShedRoof3" /></a> <br /> </p>

<p>I was particularly chuffed, and even rather impressed to see that in Hertfordshire apparently &quot;just under 70 per cent of the county&#39;s household waste was sent for re-use, recycling or composting&quot; in April and June. AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Blank Page When Printing PDFs from Google Chrome
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: blank-page-when-printing-pdfs-from-google-chrome
CATEGORY: Web/Tech

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/09/blank-page-when-printing-pdfs-from-google-chrome.html 
DATE: 09/25/2009 09:26:02 AM
-----
BODY:
<p>When I print a PDF straight from Google&#39;s Chrome web browser I get a blank page with just the header and footer (URL etc.) and nothing else. This is what happens when using the &quot;Print...&quot; command in the &#39;page&#39; menu - the menu to the right of the address bar with a page icon.</p><p>This can be worked around by instead right-clicking on the PDF body itself and selecting &quot;Print...&quot; which takes you through Adobe&#39;s own print dialogs and gives the correct result.</p>

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Moth Identification - Large Ranunculus
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: moth-identification-large-ranunculus-3
CATEGORY: Nature
CATEGORY: Photography

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/09/moth-identification-large-ranunculus-3.html 
DATE: 09/18/2009 11:17:40 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>I found a medium size moth on the wall a couple of days ago and decided I&#39;d try and figure out exactly what it was. I was already aware that there are many more species of moth as there are butterfly - something like 2,000+ in the UK apparently.</p><p>I started off by taking some up-close and personal photos of my moth, which was about 25mm long head to wing tip. Then I pored through my large &quot;Butterflies &amp; Moths in Britain and Europe&quot; book, recently acquired at a charity shop mainly to assist with butterfly identification. The only way to use this book when you have no idea what you&#39;re looking at is to flick through from cover to cover looking for a matching photograph. Then do the same again just in case you missed it. I was looking for a relatively dull, mottled brown beast with stripy legs, but I didn&#39;t find it.</p><p></p><p class="asset asset-image"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a5814ac6970b-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="text-align: center;display: block; "><img alt="LargeRanunculusMoth" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e015888340120a5814ac6970b " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a5814ac6970b-400wi" style="width: 400px; margin: 0px;" /></a></p><p></p><p>I turned to the web and quickly found the rather excellent <a href="http://www.google.com/url?sa=t&amp;source=web&amp;ct=res&amp;cd=1&amp;url=http%3A%2F%2Fukmoths.org.uk%2F&amp;ei=ZwK0SsPYL4mG4gbj55B9&amp;usg=AFQjCNHP__QMedAmSuHVGb0a-k2uzUhUYA" target="_blank">UK Moths</a> website, complete with keyword search. Unfortunately &quot;mottled brown&quot; and &quot;mottled grey&quot; didn&#39;t quite do the trick, returning tens of results but none of the quite what I was after. Lots of moths fit this very vague description so it&#39;s a tough one to solve with a simple text search. The best match I could find was the <a href="http://ukmoths.org.uk/show.php?id=3307" target="_blank">Grey Chi</a>, but I wasn&#39;t convinced as that&#39;s much more silvery and lacks the small orange markings, though I wondered if it could be put down to variability between individuals. So I turned to the site&#39;s creator Ian and fired off an image and description to the email address given (only to be used once all other avenues exhausted). He got back to me within a couple of days to reveal that it is in fact a&#0160;<a href="http://www.ukmoths.org.uk/show.php?id=1104" target="_blank">Large Ranunculus</a> - and yes I think he&#39;s bang on. This is a man who knows his moths!</p><p></p>
-----

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Fridge Temperature Control
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: fridge-temperature-control
CATEGORY: Design
CATEGORY: Food and Drink
CATEGORY: Web/Tech

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/09/fridge-temperature-control.html 
DATE: 09/17/2009 08:09:39 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>The temperature controls in most fridges really get my design goat. Are they a thermostatic &#0160;&#39;temperature&#39; control or a &#39;power&#39; control? They&#39;re not giving anything away! If I want my fridge to be colder should I turn up the control to 5 for maximum cooling power, or turn it down to 1 as in 1 degree centigrade? Labelling it 1 to 5 is just begging for confusion. If it&#39;s truly a thermostat (and well enough calibrated) then make it clear with &#39;c&#39; markings. If it&#39;s a power control then make that clear with &quot;cooler&quot; / &quot;warmer&quot;, red / blue gradients or something. Perhaps I need to buy more expensive fridges with digital thermostatic controls.</p><p style="text-align: center;"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a5d1155f970c-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="FridgeControl" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e015888340120a5d1155f970c " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a5d1155f970c-400wi" style="width: 400px; " /></a> </p>

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Beer Review: Badger Long Days
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: beer-review-badger-long-days
CATEGORY: Beer
CATEGORY: Food and Drink

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/09/beer-review-badger-long-days.html 
DATE: 09/16/2009 08:45:30 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>Long Days has a hint of raspberry to make an interesting summer brew. Golden in colour and 4.5% ABV it&#39;s nicely weighted for a summer&#39;s day and the raspberry is not so much as to become cloying, but enough to make it stand apart from the competition.</p><p>I&#39;m a touch annoyed by the labelling on the bottle, which tells us that &quot;to celebrate the summer solstice in the past, ale was often brewed with raspberry leaves as an alleged aid to fertility&quot; but only mentions a &quot;subtle hint of raspberries&quot;, in such a manner that I suspect they didn&#39;t achieve it by adding the raspberry leaves they evocatively mention. I imagine that if they did then they&#39;d have been clear about it, so they probably get the raspberry flavour into the beer in a less romantic manner - perhaps by adding juice. Labelling like this always leaves me feeling like the brewer has tried to con me with their carefully chosen words, which is a shame as it&#39;s a good beer.</p><p style="text-align: center;"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a5cc3c49970c-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="LongDays" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e015888340120a5cc3c49970c " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a5cc3c49970c-350wi" style="width: 350px; " /></a> </p>

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Mighty Mouse Ball Cleaning
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: mighty-mouse-ball-cleaning
CATEGORY: DIY
CATEGORY: Mac

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/09/mighty-mouse-ball-cleaning.html 
DATE: 09/15/2009 10:54:27 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>Every few months the scroll ball on my <a href="http://www.apple.com/mightymouse/" target="_blank">Apple Mighty Mouse</a>&#0160;starts to get a bit intermittent because of the build up of dirt, fibres and grease in the mechanism, which is very frustrating. For the past few days I&#39;ve only been able to scroll up, and reading web pages backwards is losing its novelty. There are a million and one web pages out there telling you how best to clean your ball, and I&#39;ve tried several of them.</p><p>Some people suggest <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Jet7488UoSE" target="_blank">taking the mouse apart</a>, but that apparently incurs a high risk of cracking it, requiring gluing back together, and is clearly an all round monumental faff, so I count it as an option of last resort which thankfully I&#39;ve not had to employ yet.</p><p>Running a fine piece of sticky tape under the ball and flossing was a particularly delicate operation but didn&#39;t make much difference, so I don&#39;t recommend that.</p><p>Turning the mouse upside down and simply <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=o0z3fStz4Zo" target="_blank">rolling the ball around on a clean piece of paper</a> has the beauty of immediacy and simplicity and certainly helps a bit, but not if you&#39;ve got major problems.</p><p>Best of all is the application of WD40 (or even vodka as one German YouTuber advocates) then a good roll around with a clean rag. The idea is to get your cleaning fluid all around the ball so it cleans the rollers underneath, dissolving the grease and lifting fibres, so I recommend long circular movements in many directions, trying to get the ball going every which way. A second application may be required. Don&#39;t use too much fluid though or it may wreak havoc with the inside of your mouse. WD40 is just viscose enough, and easily sprayed on in a small quantity, so it&#39;s controllable. It sorts me out every time.</p><p style="text-align: center;"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a5c8c1ee970c-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="MightyMouseBall" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e015888340120a5c8c1ee970c " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a5c8c1ee970c-400wi" style="width: 400px; " /></a> </p><p></p><p></p>

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Chafer Grub in my Soil
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: chafer-grub-in-my-soil
CATEGORY: Nature

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/09/chafer-grub-in-my-soil.html 
DATE: 09/14/2009 11:04:59 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>Digging in the borders of my new garden has revealed all sorts of interesting life. I found a few of these grubs, which are probably <a href="http://www.letsgogardening.co.uk/Pests/Chafer.htm" target="_blank">Chafer Beetle Larvae</a>. Apparently these are a common pest in lawns, eating grass roots from several inches under the soil. The first picture is poor, but gives you the general idea of the curled up shape they adopt.</p><p style="text-align: center;"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a56ee62d970b-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="SoilGrub 2" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e015888340120a56ee62d970b " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a56ee62d970b-350wi" style="width: 350px; " /></a>&#0160;<a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a5c58ae7970c-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="SoilGrub 1" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e015888340120a5c58ae7970c " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a5c58ae7970c-350wi" style="width: 350px; " /></a> </p>

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Female Lesser Stag Beetle (or is it a Stag Beetle?)
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: female-lesser-stag-beetle-or-is-it-a-stag-beetle
CATEGORY: Nature
CATEGORY: Photography

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/09/female-lesser-stag-beetle-or-is-it-a-stag-beetle.html 
DATE: 09/09/2009 11:14:59 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>We found this rather large beetle on the bedroom floor a few weeks back, which was a bit unexpected. However it seemed to be on its last legs and by the look of it was a bit gunged up with spider web and carpet fibres. I can&#39;t make up my mind whether it&#39;s a stag beetle or lesser stag beetle, though it&#39;s definitely a female. There are <a href="http://maria.fremlin.de/stagbeetles/photos_dp.html" target="_blank">some decent pages</a> out there trying to help in making this identification, but it&#39;s still not quite clear to me. If I had to put money on it I&#39;d go for lesser stag, because it&#39;s very black and seems to have some sort of ridges on its forelegs. I wish I&#39;d paid greater attention to the size at the time!</p><p style="text-align: center;"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a5b4b523970c-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="StagBeetle" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e015888340120a5b4b523970c " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a5b4b523970c-400wi" style="width: 400px; " /></a> </p>

TITLE: Hedgehog Poo
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: hedgehog-poo
CATEGORY: Nature

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/09/hedgehog-poo.html 
DATE: 09/07/2009 04:15:01 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>I&#39;ve seen a couple of droppings on the lawn over the last week that I assumed might be cat, or maybe fox, but I&#39;ve come to the conclusion that it&#39;s almost definitely hedgehog. They&#39;re very dark, sticky and show evidence of bits of beetle. Though according to my research you&#39;d expect worms, fruit and seeds to be a major constituent too - which could well be the case here.</p><p>We have seen a hedgehog snuffling around the borders so it seems like a reasonable leap of logic. Cats don&#39;t tend to go on open grass, much preferring the freshly dug earth of the vegetable patch. There&#39;s not much for the urban fox in our back garden, and I&#39;d expect bigger doings from such an animal anyway. I wonder if you can toilet train a hedgehog...</p><p style="text-align: center;"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a5537cc0970b-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="Hedgehog Poo" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e015888340120a5537cc0970b " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a5537cc0970b-400wi" style="width: 400px; " /></a> </p>

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Millipede
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: millipede
CATEGORY: Nature
CATEGORY: Photography

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/09/millipede.html 
DATE: 09/06/2009 09:29:52 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>I was digging the borders in the garden this afternoon, and amidst the stones, buried crazy paving pathway and weeds I found some interesting bugs. First up, a millipede, though I couldn&#39;t tell you what sort. My brief research suggests there are at least 50 UK species of millipede and they can be quite hard to tell apart. It was about 30mm long I&#39;d say.</p><p style="text-align: center;"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a5a74930970c-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="Millipede 2" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e015888340120a5a74930970c " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a5a74930970c-400wi" style="width: 400px; " /></a> </p><p style="text-align: left;">I got him side on from low down in this second shot, to see the little legs working away underneath in a wave like motion up the body. Millipedes have two pairs of legs per body section, easily seen here, whereas centipedes only have one pair per section. As always, click for bigger version. That&#39;s a gardening book in the background - we have a lot to learn!</p><p style="text-align: center;"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a550b6cb970b-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="Millipede 1" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e015888340120a550b6cb970b " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a550b6cb970b-600wi" style="width: 600px; " /></a> </p>

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Snow Leopard Arrives
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: snow-leopard-arrives
CATEGORY: Design
CATEGORY: Mac
CATEGORY: Web/Tech

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/09/snow-leopard-arrives.html 
DATE: 09/05/2009 11:54:41 AM
-----
BODY:
<p>Precisely one week after it was launched, my copy of Mac OS X 10.6 &quot;Snow Leopard&quot; landed on my desk at work. Apple claim to have posted it last Friday, but the bank holiday weekend and postal strikes have conspired to keep me waiting this long.</p>

<p>On my recent Mac Pro it installed in 28 minutes and recovered a startling 31GB of disk space. I&#39;m not quite sure how it managed that to be honest, as it&#39;s a lot more than most others are reporting. [<strong>Update:</strong> actually I suspect it&#39;s because Apple have changed the definition of a GB for Snow Leopard, so my comparisons of space used before and after are not comparing like for like. Now 1GB = 10^9 = 1,000,000,000 bytes, whereas previously it was 2^10 * 2^10 * 2^10 = 1024 * 1024 * 1024 = 1,073,741,824 bytes.]</p><p>That same Mac Pro is also capable of booting into the 64 bit kernel by holding down &#39;6&#39; and &#39;4&#39; during boot. You can check it&#39;s worked in System Profiler, where on the Software page it should say&#0160;&#0160;&quot;64-bit Kernel and Extensions: Yes&quot;. I&#39;ve not noticed any abnormalities and supposedly it might run a bit faster this way, so if it stays good then&#0160;I&#39;ll probably set it to 64 bit kernel permanently.</p><p>Note that only XServe machines boot with the 64 bit kernel by default, and many 64 bit Macs (like older Core 2 Duo MacBooks) can&#39;t do so because they lack 64 bit EFI (Extensible Firmware Interface).</p><p style="text-align: center;"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a54b21db970b-pi" style="display: inline;"><img alt="SnowLeopardDockMenu" border="0" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e015888340120a54b21db970b " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a54b21db970b-800wi" title="SnowLeopardDockMenu" /></a> </p><p>In general I like Snow Leopard - it&#39;s the same as Leopard but all round snappier and a bit nicer. Some changes confuse me though. Take the new arbitrarily styled menus for dock items, as shown below. Nothing else in the system looks the same, and that&#39;s probably a good thing because it&#39;s hard to read, with the section heads and tick marks being far too low contrast. They&#39;re almost invisible! A real UI own goal if you ask me. Maybe they designed it before they <a href="/atc/2009/06/snow-leopard-gamma-22.html" target="_blank">set the gamma to 2.2</a>...</p>
-----

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: House / Bath Spider: Tegenaria Duellica (AKA Tegenaria Gigantea)
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: house-bath-spider-tegenaria-duellica-aka-tegenaria-gigantea
CATEGORY: Nature
CATEGORY: Photography

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/09/house-bath-spider-tegenaria-duellica-aka-tegenaria-gigantea.html 
DATE: 09/02/2009 10:33:30 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>It&#39;s starting to get wet and wild outside as autumn replaces summer and that means it&#39;s time for big brown spiders in the bath. Here&#39;s one that Mrs C was delighted to find last night. Click for scarier, larger version!</p><p style="text-align: center;"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a598dd40970c-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="BathSpider (1)" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e015888340120a598dd40970c " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a598dd40970c-400wi" style="width: 400px; " /></a> </p><p style="text-align: left;">A bit of research suggests this is an example of <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Giant_house_spider" target="_blank">Tegenaria Duellica - i.e. Common House Spider</a> in UK parlance. There seems to be a bit of confusion out there on the web (ho ho) as to the many close varieties of Tegenaria, but I think consensus is that Duellica and Gigantea are in fact the same thing, with Gigantea being the deprecated nomenclature.</p><p style="text-align: left;">This example is about 6cm across the legs, with perhaps a 16mm body. The long legs and slender body suggest it&#39;s a male, which makes sense as it&#39;s the males out roaming for a mate at this time of year, which is why we see so many of them all of a sudden.</p>

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Bats in Verulamium Park
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: bats-in-verulamium-park
CATEGORY: Culture
CATEGORY: Nature

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/08/bats-in-verulamium-park.html 
DATE: 08/28/2009 10:45:40 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>Last night we went down to Verulamium Park to watch bats. That&#39;s&#0160;the big park in St Albans with river, lake, trees, Roman ruins etc. It was also a marvellous opportunity to refresh ourselves with the occasional ale from different pubs along the way, but that&#39;s by the by.</p>

<p>At half eight we emerged from the Fighting Cocks (a contender for Britain&#39;s oldest pub, though a weak one I think) and sure enough we were surrounded by swooping bats by the edge of the lake, emerging from the trees. It was pretty dark, but you could just about see them silhouetted against the dim sky. There were a fair few of them, and sometimes just passing by your face, apparently oblivious to our presence.</p><p style="text-align: center;"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a583044f970c-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="VerulamiumBat" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e015888340120a583044f970c " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a583044f970c-350wi" style="width: 350px; " /></a> </p>

<p>I took my camera, knowing that it was rather optimistic. I set to ISO 1600 (or 3200, or even higher at times) and f2.8 using a 105mm lens and quickly discovered that flash was an absolute necessity, not surprisingly. The on-camera flash (I don&#39;t have an external unit) allowed me to keep the shutter speed around 1/200s but still at super-high ISO. However I had to fix the focus manually at a distance about 4 yards ahead and aim extremely approximately with the camera away from my eye. It was quite impossible to see and track anything through the viewfinder, so it really was pot luck firing into the gloom as I saw one pass by. Most shots were of blank, black sky. A few included a small blob, blurry from both motion and incorrect focus. However I did luck out and get one shot that was head and shoulders above the rest. It&#39;s clearly a bat, though you can&#39;t say much more than that. You should have seen the rejects.</p>
-----

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Speckled Wood Butterfly (as an iPhone Macro test)
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: speckled-wood-butterfly-as-an-iphone-macro-test
CATEGORY: iPhone
CATEGORY: Nature
CATEGORY: Photography

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/08/speckled-wood-butterfly-as-an-iphone-macro-test.html 
DATE: 08/23/2009 08:52:37 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>I happened across a Speckled Wood butterfly on our apple tree, that apparently didn&#39;t mind me shoving an iPhone about two inches from its delicate self. It was well into a sunny day so I didn&#39;t expect it to be so docile.</p>

<p style="text-align: center;"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a514612c970b-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="SpeckledWoodButterfly" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e015888340120a514612c970b selected " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a514612c970b-400wi" style="width: 400px; " /></a> </p>

<p>It also made for an interesting test of iPhone macro camera capability. The results in this picture are fair, though it has smeared the subtle feathery detail in the wing quite badly. I suppose that&#39;s to be expected from such a tiny sensor, with lots of anti-noise processing to compensate. The biggest difficulty I found was getting it to reliably focus on the point I was interested in, resulting in lots of shots of an in-focus leaf and a blurry butterfly. Theoretically you can tap the screen to indicate the point for focussing and metering, but I didn&#39;t find that to work particularly well. Worst of all it doesn&#39;t give any obvious positive or negative feedback on whether it thinks it has successfully locked on or not. I&#39;d like it to flash a green square when it&#39;s got a good AF lock, and maybe a red disintegrating one if it has failed.</p>

<p>Note that this is a crop from the original. Click for higher res. Another major annoyance of the iPhone&#39;s Camera app is that when viewing the photos, it shows a low-res blurry version when zoomed in, leading you to think that the camera is significantly worse than it is, and making is very difficult to check focus. I really can&#39;t understand why they&#39;d do this!</p>
-----

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: BarclayCard Website Improvements
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: barclaycard-website-improvements
CATEGORY: Current Affairs
CATEGORY: Design
CATEGORY: Web/Tech

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/08/barclaycard-website-improvements.html 
DATE: 08/22/2009 07:41:12 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>I was pleasantly surprised when I went to pay my most recent credit card bill. Not only was it relatively small for a change, but the BarclayCard website has been revamped, with that most unusual of results: a markedly better user experience!</p><p>They now show a coloured bar meter indicating your total credit limit (the whole length of the bar) with your last statement and current total outstanding clearly marked as coloured portions of it. It&#39;s a really great way to graphically show the balance. They&#39;ve clearly paid attention to every aspect of user interaction, with the flow being very straightforward and very clearly guided at all times, but not onerous.</p><p>Perhaps the very best change is the return of the option to pay off your last statement in full. For the last year or so they had things set up so the options when paying were: minimum amount, whole balance (including new transactions since last statement) or custom amount. To pay off your last statement in full you had to manually read off the amount and type it into the custom field. This was very cheeky of them, clearly trying to steer the punters into taking less advantage of the free credit grace period (by paying more than their last statement amount) or paying less than their last statement amount and so accruing expensive interest. I&#39;m glad to see this cynical move has been reversed.</p>

TITLE: Anglesey Abbey, Gardens and Lode Mill

<p>A good few weeks back now, we visited <a href="http://www.nationaltrust.org.uk/main/w-vh/w-visits/w-findaplace/w-angleseyabbeyandgardenandlodemill.htm" target="_blank">Anglesey Abbey, Gardens and Lode Mill</a> - a National Trust property near Cambridge. As usual no photos of the house (it&#39;s not allowed) so you&#39;ll have to take it on trust that it was an enchanting time-warp covering the last several centuries, with a warm, lived-in feeling.</p>

<p>The gardens were large and diverse, with natural woodland, formal gardens, meadows and everything in-between. There was a strong emphasis on nature, with many habitats set up to encourage wildlife. In one corner runs the river smothered in lily pads, to Lode Mill - an interesting building in its own right, but sadly the gear wasn&#39;t working when we were there. Moorhen chicks ran across the leafy surface of the river seldom touching the water and Banded Demoiselle damselflies glinted in the sun.</p><p>Onto the pictures! First, a rather fun door in the middle of the woods, followed by a Painted Lady butterfly at the edge of the dew pond.</p>

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Siemens Dishwasher Door
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: siemens-dishwasher-door
CATEGORY: Design
CATEGORY: Food and Drink

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/08/siemens-dishwasher-door.html 
DATE: 08/17/2009 07:00:39 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>When is a Dishwasher door not a dishwasher door? When it&#39;s a jar.</p><p>That&#39;s a joke by the way. It&#39;s especially a joke if you have a Siemens dishwasher who&#39;s door is not designed to be left ajar.&#0160;You can have it fully open, or fully closed, but it won&#39;t rest in any position in-between unless you prop it open, e.g. with a cork or other handy item that you may have to hand, as per my picture below.</p>
<p>Why would I want to prop it open? Because after it&#39;s finished, if you open the door for 15 minutes then the residual heat dries the contents just nicely, as long as the steam can escape. If you don&#39;t open the door, you can look forward to plates and glasses that still need the attention of a tea towel, even several hours after the machine finishes its cycle. Leaving the door fully open is asking for a kitchen accident of course, so that&#39;s not really an option. This door ajar approach is standard practice with any dishwasher, no? Maybe I&#39;m alone in this, but every other dishwasher I&#39;ve come across neatly sits open a few inches to facilitate my whim, and it&#39;s got to be trivially easy to manufacture into the door mechanism. Certainly my posh Siemens dishwasher would look a lot better without the cork.</p><p style="text-align: center;"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a4fe790c970b-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="DishwasherCork" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e015888340120a4fe790c970b " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a4fe790c970b-400wi" style="width: 400px; " /></a> </p>

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/08/beer-review-arkells-3b.html 
DATE: 08/11/2009 07:28:54 PM

BODY:
<p>A mobile beer review today! Who says variety is dead?</p><p>Here we see pictured the can of Arkell&#39;s 3B that quenched my frazzled business brain after a hard day out of the office a month or so ago. This was on a train back from Swindon to London to be precise, and I have to say that the availability of a half decent drop of bitter on the train was a pleasant surprise. <a href="http://www.arkells.com/" target="_blank">Arkell&#39;s</a> is actually a Swindon based brewery too, so it&#39;s nice to see the big nasty train company keeping the food miles down and offering local producers.</p><p>It&#39;s got a decent colour to it, and the well rounded maltiness you&#39;d hope to find from that colour. At 4% the weight is just about right for the circumstances. All in all it was very welcome and dare I say even recommended if you find yourself near Swindon on a train, even out of a small plastic cup!</p><p style="text-align: center;"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a4e5a4bd970b-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="Arkells3B" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e015888340120a4e5a4bd970b " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a4e5a4bd970b-400wi" style="width: 400px; " /></a> </p>

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: iPhone Calendar Entry - Change Calendar
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: iphone-calendar-entry-change-calendar
CATEGORY: iPhone
CATEGORY: Mac

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/08/iphone-calendar-entry-change-calendar.html 
DATE: 08/09/2009 08:36:34 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>I&#39;ve noticed that in iPhone&#39;s Calendar, you can&#39;t change the calendar (Home,Work, etc.) of an entry once it&#39;s been created - only at the point that it is being created. This is immensely frustrating as quite often I fail to spot which calendar an entry is being created in until after I&#39;ve hit Done and I see it showing up in green or blue in my calendar. I split about 50/50 between Home and Work entries and so very often each new entry is of a different type to the last (though I fail to notice it) leaving the default calendar assignation incorrect. Grrrr.</p><p><strong>Update:</strong> I realised that a big reason for failing to spot which calendar is being used at point of entry is that it doesn&#39;t use the calendar colour in the creation UI - only the name. If it backed the name with a big splash of colour (green for home, blue for work) I for one would be far less likely to mess up.</p>

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Creating a Grub Screw for a Doorknob
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: creating-a-grub-screw-for-a-doorknob
CATEGORY: DIY

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/08/creating-a-grub-screw-for-a-doorknob.html 
DATE: 08/07/2009 10:53:35 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>This old house has lots of old door knobs, but some are a bit worse for wear. I&#39;ve already repaired a broken spring in one with some cobbled together bits from an old wooden clothes peg, but that&#39;s another story. Another was lacking a crucial grub screw that meant the knob on one side just rotated freely, rather than operating the latch. The nice guy at Alban Locksmiths furnished me with an Imperial threaded screw that fits. However I needed a grub screw - one where there is no &#39;head&#39; so to speak so that it can worm its way right into the hole.</p>

<p>No problem! Just saw the head off the normal screw then saw a notch in the end for the screwdriver. Here&#39;s a pictorial essay of my approach, the only trick of any merit being to clamp the screw between two bits of soft wood in the vice, so that it&#39;s gripped securely and you can saw it without it slipping or being damaged.</p><p style="text-align: center;"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a52ae9b0970c-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="GrubScrew 1" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e015888340120a52ae9b0970c " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a52ae9b0970c-300wi" style="width: 300px; " /></a>&#0160;&#0160;<a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a52ae9ee970c-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="GrubScrew 2" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e015888340120a52ae9ee970c " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a52ae9ee970c-300wi" style="width: 300px; " /></a> </p><p style="text-align: center;"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a4d3e02e970b-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="GrubScrew 3" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e015888340120a4d3e02e970b " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a4d3e02e970b-300wi" style="width: 300px; AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Update iPhone Software Using Internet Tethering: Don't!
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: update-iphone-software-using-internet-tethering-dont
CATEGORY: iPhone
CATEGORY: Mac
CATEGORY: Web/Tech

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/08/update-iphone-software-using-internet-tethering-dont.html 
DATE: 08/05/2009 06:04:44 PM
-----
BODY:
<div>Because my broadband wasn&#39;t working I&#39;ve been using internet tethering with my iPhone for my main internet connection for my computer. So when my iPhone demanded I update its software to cure its SMS vulnerability I thought hey why not go ahead! I figured it would download the update to the computer (via the iPhone&#39;s net connection) as per normal, then perform the update. No reason to suspect a problem.&#0160;</div><br /><div>Unfortunately once it had got the whole 300MB package and tried to install it, it required access to some Apple server in order to finish the install, but the iPhone was half-updated and no longer providing internet connectivity. So I got stuck there, with an iPhone just showing a &quot;connect to iTunes&quot; graphic when switched on. I understand this is known as &quot;<a href="http://mickerlodeon.com/2009/03/iphone-recovery-mode-how-to/" target="_blank">recovery mode</a>&quot;. And that&#39;s how it&#39;s been for a full day, but thankfully I now have broadband working and have managed to get it back up on its feet. That required a factory restore then update from backup then full sync though, and I&#39;m yet to determine if all is truly well.</div><br /><div>So the lesson here is - don&#39;t use your iPhone as the sole internet connection in order to update your iPhone!</div>
-----

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: iPhone Internet Tethering: GIF and JPEG quality
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: iphone-internet-tethering-gif-and-jpeg-quality
CATEGORY: iPhone
CATEGORY: Mac
CATEGORY: Web/Tech

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/08/iphone-internet-tethering-gif-and-jpeg-quality.html 
DATE: 08/04/2009 01:44:26 PM
-----
BODY:
<div>For some reason, having switched it off when the previous occupants left, we now have to wait 2 weeks for BT to turn our broadband back on again. I know not why. They must literally have a system that includes a &quot;wait two weeks for no good reason&quot; step. As such I&#39;m using my iPhone with internet tethering as my internet connection.</div><br /><div>It works reasonably well, maxing out at about 50 kilobytes/s - which equates to about half a megabit, so stretching the term broadband quite thin but useable as long as you&#39;re not in a hurry. However I&#39;ve noticed that O2 are pulling a fast one (pun intended) and rewriting JPEG and GIF images that you request via HTTP, re-encoding them at a much lower quality level, presumably in order to make your bandwidth go that much further.</div><br /><div>I have a problem with this though as they&#39;ve gone so far down the quality slope that the images are often no longer fit for purpose, with small text unreadable and photos suffering from JPEG artefacts so badly that there&#39;s only a muddy mess left. Here&#39;s a small screenshot from my blog sidebar, showing the knackered JPEG, which I have saved with very high quality JPEG compression so as not to introduce more artefacts. Of course when I review this post it&#39;ll get re-compressed by O2 again and look even more terrible (indeed the hyperlink text is near unreadable) but hopefully you won&#39;t have that problem unless you&#39;re also tethering.</div><br /><div style="text-align: center;"><img alt="O2CompressedJPEG" border="0" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e015888340120a51c7d5e970c " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340120a51c7d5e970c-800wi" title="O2CompressedJPEG" /><br /></div><br /><div>So this is a plea to O2, asking them to turn up the quality, if they must mess with the web at all.</div>

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: DIY Jobs
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: diy-jobs
CATEGORY: DIY

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/07/diy-jobs.html 
DATE: 07/31/2009 08:09:37 PM
-----
BODY:
<div>We&#39;ve been in the new house for just a week and have done a lot in that time. Here&#39;s a quick list of most of the DIY jobs we&#39;ve done - with a bit of help from the parents and in-laws. Thanks very much to them!</div><br /><div><div>Cleaning - lots thereof.</div><div>Fill crack in front door panel, that you could see outside through.</div><div>Trim holly and other bushy plant that was half blocking drive.</div><div>Remove dead and scrappy bits of Goldenrod and tie back with string (later replaced with green wire).</div><div>Brush whole deck with stiff brush to clean it up.</div><div>Remove posts and chains from most of deck edge.</div><div>Fit new lock to front door (got existing one refurbished and innards replaced).</div><div>Fit retaining bar to front door.</div><div>Fit coat hook rail to wall in hall.</div><div>Put up pan hanger rail in kitchen.</div><div>Replace hooks on back of bedroom door for nicer ones.</div><div>Figure out why living room door knob isn&#39;t working the latch - needs a grub screw.</div><div>Put up new curtain rod in master bedroom, reusing existing holes (needed some adaptation).</div><div>Fit new keyhole escutcheon with cover (on inside of front door, to get the benefit, without the annoyance).</div><div>Put together flat pack metal shelving from Homebase. 56 nuts and bolts! Won&#39;t buy that again.</div><div>Improve sink in bathroom, raising it on bits of card and screwing it better to the wall, for a flusher fit. Still needs grout and seal.</div><div>Adjust patio door hanging to help it close properly.</div><div>Adjust cabin door hanging to help it close properly.</div><div>Sweep patio around cabin, including leaves and crud at back, that could have caused damp.</div><div>Fix shower so it doesn&#39;t leak: remove old sealant, chip away years of limescale, clean, regrout and reseal. (Still working on this actually, but it&#39;s the biggest job of any of them time-wise.)</div><div>Clean UPVC outdoor bits of patio doors using special cleaner.</div><div>Fit extra shelf under kitchen sink by cutting out section of original extra shelf to fit round drain pipes etc.</div><div>Fit cleat to tree stump and run washing line to apple tree (where held with wide strap round tree).</div><div>Fit bird feeder hanger to tree stump.</div><div>Saw off and file down ends from over-long bolts protruding from chimney back plate in kitchen.</div><div>Fit lock to side window.</div><div>Put up IKEA mirror in bathroom, with cunning springy top-clasps.</div><div>Assemble IKEA shelves for computery stuff.</div></div>

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Useless O2 Internet Tethering Bolt On
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: useless-o2-internet-tethering-bolt-on
CATEGORY: iPhone

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/07/useless-o2-internet-tethering-bolt-on.html 
DATE: 07/20/2009 10:19:19 PM
-----
BODY:
<div>I had a couple of long train journeys today, so this morning just after I boarded that train at Paddington I followed the instructions on my iPhone to turn on <a href="http://shop.o2.co.uk/update/internet.html" target="_blank">internet tethering</a>. This would allow me to use its 3G internet connection on my laptop via bluetooth, enabling me to get some work done. Brilliant!</div><br /><div>Follow the instructions to enable it and you end up with a fiddly web form that requires you to manually fill in the details that O2 already have for you. How&#39;s that for an integrated experience?! Terrible, that&#39;s how. And then the coup de grace - it&#39;s 14 hours later and internet tethering has still not been turned on for my phone. Both train journeys have been and gone, I&#39;m starved of juicy internet goodness and O2 are presumably laughing at me whilst making a small tower from 15 of my pound coins.</div><br /><div>Their instructions do say it could take up to 24 hours to come alive, but it&#39;s natural to assume that this is a worst case caveat, like Royal Mail saying you&#39;re not allowed to complain about 1st class mail until it&#39;s gone missing for 7 days - a backup clause to cover exceptional circumstances. Apparently O2 are serious, perhaps to deliberately discourage people who are in any way impulsive from stupidly parting with their money for such an overpriced service. Perhaps they&#39;re on our side after all...</div><br /><div><strong>Update:</strong> about 30 hours have now passed since I bought the tethering bolt on. Now not only does my phone still not have data tethering, but it has no data connection whatsoever. So I can&#39;t get email, visual voicemail, web etc. on the phone itself, let alone on a tethered device. A quick call to O2&#39;s magic iPhone support number gives me a recorded message that they&#39;re having trouble in the London area with &#39;network congestion&#39;. I don&#39;t see why this innocuous Tuesday would result in a tidal wave of traffic that brings their service to its knees, unless it&#39;s simply the continuing weight of iPhones being added to its network every day as they continue to sell like hotcakes.</div>

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/07/woodlouse-spider.html 
DATE: 07/18/2009 11:15:25 PM
-----
BODY:
<div>Look what <a href="http://mrsc.typepad.co.uk/" target="_blank">Mrs C</a> found in the bathroom today! A very large <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Woodlouse_spider" target="_blank">woodlouse spider</a> - at least 25mm including legs, which seems to be as large as they come. I&#39;ve seen smaller ones before, about half this size. Yes, this picture was taken through the side of the pint glass that I put over it! These slightly scary spiders have very large bitey things at the front (technical term&#0160;chelicerae) and can give a nasty nip apparently, though are unlikely to.</div><br /><div style="text-align: center;"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e0158883401157122ae9e970c-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="WoodlouseSpider" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e0158883401157122ae9e970c " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e0158883401157122ae9e970c-400wi" style="width: 400px; " /></a> <br /></div>

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Beer Review: Fuller's HoneyDew
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: beer-review-fullers-honeydew
CATEGORY: Beer
CATEGORY: Food and Drink

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/07/beer-review-fullers-honeydew.html 
DATE: 07/14/2009 08:24:59 PM
-----
BODY:
<div>I can&#39;t believe I haven&#39;t reviewed this before now as it&#39;s a classic and a firm favourite of mine. At 5% ABV and with just enough honey to notice but not overpower, this is a well balanced brew. This is true in every sense with not too much bitterness either - just enough to counter the &#0160;sweetness. It doesn&#39;t taste as alcoholic as it is and I reckon it&#39;s a perfect if-you&#39;re-going-to-have-just-one-beer-in-an-evening beverage. I prefer it reasonably chilled - more so than less sweet ales - which probably makes me a philistine, but so be it. It&#39;s quite similar in style to some of the more floral, sweet and spicy Badger beers, of which I am also a huge fan.</div><br /><div style="text-align: center;"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340115710fe117970c-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="HoneydewBeer" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e015888340115710fe117970c " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340115710fe117970c-400wi" style="width: 400px; " /></a> <br /></div>

<div>On a balmy summer&#39;s day (the day of the men&#39;s final at Wimbledon) we ventured back to <a href="http://www.nationaltrust.org.uk/main/w-shawscorner" target="_blank">Shaw&#39;s Corner</a> for a stroll around its beautifully relaxed gardens. This is where playwright George Bernard Shaw lived for over 40 years. The house and gardens aren&#39;t huge, but I like their style - lazy, slow, ambling and pleasant. Lawns, shady paths, vibrant flowerbeds, meadowy orchards, languid trees, and all kept in a not-too-formal style that sees the stresses ooze out of me.</div><br /><div>I only had my macro lens, so no sweeping panoramas - you&#39;ll have to take my word for it on the descriptions above, or visit the National Trust page I&#39;ve linked to for that sort of thing.</div><br /><div style="text-align: center;"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e01588834011570f25d16970c-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: iCal Event Inspector - Welcome Back!
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: ical-event-inspector-welcome-back
CATEGORY: Mac

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/07/ical-event-inspector-welcome-back.html 
DATE: 07/08/2009 09:33:53 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>I hear that Mac OS X 10.6 Snow Leopard will herald the return of the permanently visible event inspector panel in iCal. I&#39;ve really missed it for the last couple of years. Double clicking each item then clicking &quot;Edit&quot; is a major chore and I look forward to getting back to the simple old ways.</p><p>Whilst they&#39;re at it I hope they fix the basic mouse event handling so I can reliably grab and drag the edges of an event. The current behaviour seems to be based on coin flips.</p><p><strong>Update: </strong>It&#39;s not quite what I hoped unfortunately. Rather than having a fixed panel for displaying and editing the full details of the currently selected event, there is a popup window. In exactly the same manner as the Finder&#39;s Get Info window, this can also be opened as an &#39;inspector&#39; that changes to reflect the current selection. It is always a floating window above the rest of the UI rather than a built-in portion of the main iCal window like it used to be. I&#39;ve arranged my main iCal window and inspector alongside each other and thankfully they both reappear when the app is quit and reopened. So nearly, but not quite what I was after.</p>

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: How to Upgrade WordPress (on Mac OS X)
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: how-to-upgrade-wordpress-on-mac-os-x
CATEGORY: Mac
CATEGORY: Programming
CATEGORY: Web/Tech
CATEGORY: Weblogs

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/07/how-to-upgrade-wordpress-on-mac-os-x.html 
DATE: 07/05/2009 10:45:28 PM
-----
BODY:
<div>I&#39;ve been putting together a WordPress powered blog or two recently and diligently documenting the steps required, as ever. The documentation available from the WordPress site is pretty good, but sometimes it&#39;s over verbose, whilst frustratingly also stopping short of giving you exactly the details you need. So here&#39;s what works for me to upgrade an existing WordPress installation to a newer version. This is using the manual approach BTW rather than the built in auto-upgrade functionality, which asks for FTP details (of what I&#39;m not sure, and it doesn&#39;t bother to elaborate) and therefore makes a mockery of the term &#39;auto&#39;.</div><br /><div>The official instructions that got me going initially are at&#0160;<a href="http://codex.wordpress.org/Upgrading_WordPress" target="_blank">http://codex.wordpress.org/Upgrading_WordPress</a> FWIW, but I do precisely this on Mac OS X:</div><div><div><ul>
<li>Download the zipped upgrade package and unzip it&#0160;somewhere&#0160;-&#0160;e.g.&#0160;to&#0160;wordpress_upgrade&#0160;directory&#0160;for&#0160;the&#0160;sake&#0160;of&#0160;this&#0160;example.</li>
<li>Backup existing installation in full - both the wordpress directory itself and the associated MySQL DB, just in case.</li>
<li>Merge the newly downloaded package over your existing install (assumed to be a directory named wordpress here) with the following incantation at the command line, which takes advantage of the fact that cp merges, whereas Finder copying just oafishly replaces:</li>
<li><span>&gt; cp -r&#0160;</span>&#0160;wordpress_upgrade/ wordpress_original</li>
<li>Compare the new wp-config-sample.php with your existing wp-config.php (e.g. using FileMerge) to see if any new config items have been added. If so, manually add those into your&#0160;wp-config.php&#0160;file, or if easier rename the sample to&#0160;wp-config.php&#0160;and put back the DB connection and other relevant bits.</li>
<li><span>Load up the /admin page in your web browser and follow the instructions to complete&#0160;the&#0160;upgrade,&#0160;which&#0160;involves&#0160;it&#0160;upgrading&#0160;any&#0160;DB&#0160;bits,&#0160;etc.</span></li>
</ul>
</div><br /><br /></div>

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: iPhone calendar sync with MobileMe
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: markdown
ALLOW PINGS: 0
BASENAME: iphone-calendar-sync-with-mobileme
CATEGORY: iPhone

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/07/iphone-calendar-sync-with-mobileme.html 
DATE: 07/02/2009 08:51:28 AM
-----
BODY:
<p>You receive your sparkly newiPhone, plug it into your Mac, everything works - and calendars are synced. A few days later you realise that all is not well as calendar updates only make the jump when you physically connect phone to the Mac and sync, but MobileMe's supposed to sync over the air with push updates and all that jazz. Turns out you need to do the following, which isn't entirely intuitive:</p>

<ul>
<li>Perform a full physical sync to ensure all data on phone is on your Mac and therefore in the MobileMe system.</li>
<li>On the iPhone go to Settings > Mail, Contacts and Calendars</li>
<li>Select your me.com/mac.com Mail account</li>
<li>Turn on the switches for syncing contacts, calendar and bookmarks as you wish.</li>
<li>This will ask what you want to do with the data already on the phone. Select "Do not merge" and then when prompted agree that it can indeed delete the existing data from your phone.</li>
<li>Et voila, all your data is still there and changes you make on Mac or iPhone swiftly wing their way across the void to the others.</li>
</ul>

-----
EXTENDED BODY:

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: iPhone Calendar throws away half-entered data
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: 0
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: iphone-calendar-throws-away-halfentered-data
CATEGORY: iPhone

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/07/iphone-calendar-throws-away-halfentered-data.html 
DATE: 07/01/2009 08:50:51 PM
-----
BODY:
<div>I've had my iPhone for a few days now, though Orange haven't got their colourful arses in gear to supply me with the PAK code required to get my old number working yet. Looks like they're sticking to the "allow seven working days" mantra, whilst also sticking two fingers up to me. There must be a line in their systems software that says "wait 5 days" before then actually sending out the letter I need. But I digress.</div><br><div>The Calendar app on iPhone has a major flaw. If you're part way through entering a new event to the calendar and a call comes in, it simply discards all the data you'd entered. When you next open Calendar it implacably stares back at you with your events neatly listed, but no memory of what you were busy entering before you were interrupted. The same is true when you press the home button, perhaps to flick to Mail in order to get a piece of information that you wanted to add into your calendar entry. Actually this is how I discovered the problem, since I don't get many calls. This is a disaster and violates a prime iPhone app programming law: reinstate things how the user left them.</div>

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Small Magpie Moth
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: 0
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: small-magpie-moth
CATEGORY: Nature
CATEGORY: Photography

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/06/small-magpie-moth.html 
DATE: 06/28/2009 07:50:13 PM
-----
BODY:
<div>Here's a close up shot of what I think is a Small Magpie Moth drying out its wings after recently emerging. Taken on a compact camera, with reasonable results. TITLE: Helsinki: The Church in the Rock
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: helsinki-the-church-in-the-rock
CATEGORY: Culture
CATEGORY: Photography
CATEGORY: Travel

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/06/helsinki-the-church-in-the-rock.html 
DATE: 06/22/2009 09:58:08 PM
-----
BODY:
<div>We recently spent a very nice 24 hours in Helsinki, Finland before crossing the strait to Tallinn, Estonia. Helsinki is quite a modern city and its delights are subtle. We very nearly didn&#39;t go to the Church in the Rock, having failed to realise that it&#39;s one of the top tourist attractions. You wouldn&#39;t know it from the humble location in the middle of a rather nondescript residential area.</div>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<div style="text-align: center;"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340115714115f7970b-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="HelsinkiChurchRock3 7398" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e015888340115714115f7970b " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340115714115f7970b-400wi" style="width: 400px;" /></a></div>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<div>Built in the late 1960s the church is sunk into the bedrock with just a domed roof poking above the natural lie of the land. It&#39;s really not much to look at from the outside, but internally it&#39;s a symphony of modernist concrete, rough-hewn stone, glass, wood and polished copper. It really speaks craftsmanship and slightly old fashioned Scandinavian design. It also has fantastic acoustics - there was a woman playing a grand piano as we wandered around, which just set it all off perfectly.</div>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<div style="text-align: center;"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340115704bf8fb970c-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="HelsinkiChurchRock2 7397" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e015888340115704bf8fb970c " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340115704bf8fb970c-400wi" style="width: 400px;" /></a></div>
<div style="text-align: center;"></div>
<div style="text-align: center;"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340115704bf93a970c-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="HelsinkiChurchRock1 7396" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e015888340115704bf93a970c " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340115704bf93a970c-400wi" style="width: 400px;" /></a></div>
