AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Curry: Lamb in Cinnamon Scented Fenugreek Sauce
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: 0
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: curry-lamb-in-cinnamon-scented-fenugreek-sauce
CATEGORY: Food and Drink

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/01/curry-lamb-in-cinnamon-scented-fenugreek-sauce.html 
DATE: 01/04/2009 11:50:41 AM
-----
BODY:
<p>Here's my second curry adventure from the Curry Bible my wife bought me for Xmas. <a href="/atc/2008/12/butter-chicken-from-ms-curry-bible.html" target="_blank">My first attempt was Butter Chicken </a>and was thoroughly awesome. This one was just as good I'd say, and it should be given all the ingredients that went into it: 8 different herbs and spices!</p><div><br><div><div style="text-align: center;"><a style="display: inline;" href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e01588834010536a7c3c0970b-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, '_blank', 'width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0' ); return false"><img  class="at-xid-6a00e5550e01588834010536a7c3c0970b " style="width: 330px; " alt="LambFenugreek1" src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e01588834010536a7c3c0970b-350wi"></a>  <a style="display: inline;" href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e01588834010536b04ee8970c-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, '_blank', 'width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0' ); return false"><img  class="at-xid-6a00e5550e01588834010536b04ee8970c " style="width: 330px; " alt="LambFenugreek2" src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e01588834010536b04ee8970c-350wi"></a> <br></div><br><div>The hardest thing to find was dried fenugreek leaves. The supermarket didn't have any so we walked to Hatfield Road, where St Albans' Asian community has a strong presence. The first shop we tried didn't have any but the proprietor was thoroughly helpful in pointing us to his competitor down the road who "has everything". He wasn't wrong - Madina Store is an Aladdin's Cave of wonderful foodstuffs, stacked floor to ceiling. It took us a while and some assistance before finding what we wanted, though it was in a packet akin to a family size box of Cornflakes. I only needed a tablespoon! Luckily my wife spotted a much smaller box (more Kellogg's Variety pack size) on the way out so we got that. We could also have got fresh Fenugreek leaves and anything else that has ever been used in Indian cooking as far as I could tell.</div><br><div style="text-align: center;"><a style="display: inline;" href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e01588834010536b04f1a970c-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, '_blank', 'width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0' ); return false"><img  class="at-xid-6a00e5550e01588834010536b04f1a970c " style="width: 330px; " alt="LambFenugreek4" src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e01588834010536b04f1a970c-350wi"></a>  <a style="display: inline;" href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e01588834010536b04f33970c-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, '_blank', 'width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0' ); return false"><img  class="at-xid-6a00e5550e01588834010536b04f33970c " style="width: 330px; " alt="LambFenugreek3" src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e01588834010536b04f33970c-350wi"></a>
 <br></div><br><div>The cooking was relatively straightforward with all the ingredients assembled, and almost a one-pot job. Marinate the lamb cubes in red wine vinegar and salt for a bit (which quickly turns it a funny colour), make up the sauce by adding various things to a saucepan as per the recipe and leave to simmer with the meat in it for 50 minutes or so. This is the only cooking the meat gets - no frying. One issue I did have was that the cinnamon stick (only a small piece) disintegrates quite readily and is then a pain to pick out in shards whilst eating it. The recipe made no mention of the stick after adding it, so it's a mystery what was supposed to happen to it.</div><br><div>The only downer on the washing up front is that you have to use a separate pan to fry the garam masala (only 1/4 of a teaspoon of it) at the very end, before adding it to the rest. I messed this bit up by burning the spices in oil that was too hot, and had to throw it away and try that bit again. No damage done.</div><br><div>The result was served with some curried veg from Waitrose - they seem to have a new range - to bulk it out, and garlic and coriander naan. It was another great meal from the good book, though it doesn't make a great deal and needed the bulking out.</div></div></div>

CATEGORY: Me

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2009/01/world-of-goo.html 
DATE: 01/01/2009 11:04:08 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>I&#39;ve just completed the computer game <a href="http://2dboy.com/games.php" target="_blank">World of Goo</a>, having been thoroughly absorbed by it for the last week or so. I seldom play computer games, but this one hooked me good and proper. I think it&#39;s the engineer in me that always love this sort of game, as it&#39;s based on a decent 2D physics model that involves building towers, bridges and lots more out of various pieces, most of them gooey and continually swaying.</p><br /><div>The game is also an artistic tour de force: wacky, surrealistic,&#0160;humorous&#0160;and stylish. I&#39;d really struggle to pick out a weak point in fact, which is probably why it&#39;s won so many awards this past year (on Mac, PC and Wii). Best of all is the demo version contains the whole of the first chapter (out of five) and the whole game only cost me £13 to download.</div><br /><div><a href="http://worldofgoo.com/dl2.php?lk=demo" target="_blank">Download the demo</a> and have a go today!</div>

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Butter Chicken, from M&S' Curry Bible
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: butter-chicken-from-ms-curry-bible
CATEGORY: Books
CATEGORY: Food and Drink

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2008/12/butter-chicken-from-ms-curry-bible.html 
DATE: 12/29/2008 06:59:30 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>My wife bought me the <a href="http://www.marksandspencer.com/gp/product/B001DTWY1K?mnSBrand=core" target="_blank" title="Curry Bible, Marks and Spencer">Curry Bible</a> for Xmas, from Marks and Spencer - not to be confused with various other similarly named books. It&#39;s a great recipe book as it keeps things relatively simple, and contains most of my curry house favourites. It explains things in a decent manner that certainly worked for me, judging by the results!</p><div><br /><div style="text-align: center;"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340105369b38b8970b-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="ButterChicken1" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e015888340105369b38b8970b " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340105369b38b8970b-350wi" style="width: 350px; " /></a>&#0160; <a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e01588834010536a34029970c-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="ButterChicken2" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e01588834010536a34029970c " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e01588834010536a34029970c-350wi" style="width: 350px; " /></a>
 <br /></div><br /><div>I made Butter Chicken for my first attempt. This uses tandoori chicken (the nicest single foodstuff in the world) but I wasn&#39;t up for doing that entirely from scratch this time around. The supermarket didn&#39;t have any tandoori chicken ready to go though, so I bought chicken thighs (free range) and a jar of tandoori paste. Add lemon juice, salt, oil and yoghurt, mix it all up (or get wife to, as in the picture) marinate overnight in the fridge then blast in the oven to get that slightly charred surface. Then I took the chicken off the bone and used it in big chunks in the Butter Chicken recipe. I&#39;ll be doing tandoori chicken again, since it was so easy and so delicious even on its own.</div><br /><div style="text-align: center;"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340105369b398c970b-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="ButterChicken3" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e015888340105369b398c970b " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340105369b398c970b-350wi" style="width: 350px; " /></a>&#0160; <a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e01588834010536a340b3970c-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="ButterChicken4" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e01588834010536a340b3970c " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e01588834010536a340b3970c-350wi" style="width: 350px; " /></a>
 <br /></div><br /><div>I shan&#39;t bore you with the details of the recipe (or invite a copyright problem) but it wasn&#39;t crazy difficult and the results were to die for. The quality of the chicken in particular really made it stand out from usual curry house fare. I know the final picture of it on the plate just looks like an orange splat, but trust me it was great, and I couldn&#39;t be doing with garnishing with nuts and coriander sprigs.</div><br /></div>

ALLOW PINGS: 1

<p>Last Tuesday I went to <a href="http://www.thewhitelionph.co.uk/" target="_blank">The White Lion</a> pub (a preferred local of mine, but blimey that&#39;s a low-fi website if ever I saw one) to see the <a href="http://www.deadvictorians.co.uk/" target="_blank">Dead Victorians</a>. These fine chaps are quite magnificent - music hall entertainment from a bygone era crammed with interesting instruments and innuendo.</p><div>This is the second time I&#39;ve seen them, in the same venue as it happens, but both times they have been a threesome, without the elusive Pedro. I don&#39;t know why, but the good Dr. Blake doesn&#39;t seem to be in any of the publicity photos and gets nary a mention on the CD (on sale that evening for the first time) whilst appearing to be a thoroughly integral part of the band on drums, many vocals, spoons, washboard etc.</div><br /><div>I&#39;ll quite happily admit that it was seeing the Dead Victorians for the first time that tipped me over the edge and caused me to buy an&#0160;accordion. It was a pleasure to see them again, though the photos I took are shamefully poor, taken as they were from the back of a crowded but dark pub with a small compact camera. The blur sitting in front of Maestro Paul on the accordion is the good doctor playing the typewriter to accompany a&#0160;vigourous trombone rendition of the William Tell Overture.</div><br /><div style="text-align: center;"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340105368a169e970b-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="DeadVictorians" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e015888340105368a169e970b " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340105368a169e970b-400wi" style="width: 400px; " /></a>

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: First Capital Connect Thameslink Changes - December 2008
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: first-capital-connect-thameslink-changes-december-2008
CATEGORY: Current Affairs
CATEGORY: Travel

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2008/12/first-capital-connect-thameslink-changes-december-2008.html 
DATE: 12/15/2008 10:50:03 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>It&#39;s always a worrying time when the train timetables change and I find out whether my commute is going to get better or worse. First Capital Connect have been promising a lot since they bought the franchise into London (I commute from St Albans to Kentish Town) but delivering little from my point of view. Today new timetables came into effect and I longed to see those &quot;more trains&quot;, &quot;longer trains&quot;, &quot;disco carriage in every train&quot; promises fulfilled. Actually I made up one of those. Actually I&#39;d might as well have made up all of them.</p><br /><div>My main two morning trains (I don&#39;t always get the same one) are much the same, except one is now four cars instead of eight. The reason I went for these trains in the first place was that they were eight car so I&#39;d get to London without being crushed. Oh well.</div><br /><div>My evening trains appear unchanged. Between 1802 and 1914 there are <span style="font-style: italic;">still</span> no eight car trains. So I either have to leave work before six or after seven unless I want to fight for standing space.</div><br /><div>I find it insulting that they joke about twelve car trains whilst reducing existing eight car services to four. I will find it doubly insulting in the new year when the fares leap up by inflation busting amounts same as they have each and every year before (usually 6-9%). I can only dream of the day when the whole fleet is replaced by trains with four seats across rather than five, bringing them blinking into the light of civilised society enjoyed by most of the rest of the country.</div>

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Omelette Baguette
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: omelette-baguette
CATEGORY: Food and Drink

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2008/12/omelette-baguette.html 
DATE: 12/13/2008 09:04:19 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>When the wife&#39;s away and you have to make dinner from the limited remains in the fridge, you end up with the extraordinary feast that is the omelette baguette. Frankly I&#39;m pretty proud of this creation, because it was absolutely delicious and over the top. Elvis would have approved.</p><div><br /><div><div style="text-align: center;"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e01588834010536629cec970c-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="OmeletteBaguette" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e01588834010536629cec970c " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e01588834010536629cec970c-550wi" style="width: 550px; " /></a>&#0160;<br /></div><br /><div>I made a straightforward 2 egg omelette in a small non-stick frying pan, then added grated mature cheddar and thin slices of a good dried sausage before folding over and leaving long enough for the cheese to melt and all the egg to just about cook. Incidentally, I always keep a big dried sausage in the fridge as it&#39;s perfect for slicing into lots of things: omelettes, pasta, laid on top of grilled fish, pizza or just to scoff as a Dutch style snack.</div><br /><div>The baguette was a part-baked one from Waitrose in this case. These are amazing as they have a shelf life of about a month (I don&#39;t want to know what they put in them to achieve this - I like to think it&#39;s just the airtight sterile packaging) and can be whacked in the oven for 10 minutes for fresh hot bread. Having let it cool a little I sliced it open and put my gooey omelette inside, cut into three pieces so it fit the long, narrow sandwich. I then added slices of tomato and a bit of pepper. Beautiful, but admittedly a bit of a coronary on a plate.</div></div></div>

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Book Review: Gods Behaving Badly - Marie Phillips
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: book-review-gods-behaving-badly-marie-phillips
CATEGORY: Books

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2008/12/book-review-gods-behaving-badly-marie-phillips.html 
DATE: 12/07/2008 01:40:33 PM
-----
BODY:
<iframe frameborder="0" marginheight="0" marginwidth="0" scrolling="no" src="http://rcm-uk.amazon.co.uk/e/cm?t=alwthecri-21&amp;o=2&amp;p=8&amp;l=as1&amp;asins=0099513021&amp;fc1=000000&amp;IS2=1&amp;lt1=_blank&amp;m=amazon&amp;lc1=0000FF&amp;bc1=000000&amp;bg1=FFFFFF&amp;f=ifr" style="float:right;margin-left:15px;margin-bottom:10px;width:120px;height:240px;"></iframe><p>

I picked this book up on a whim because I liked the sound of the basic premise. Having now read it I know for sure that it&#39;s one of the most original ideas for a novel that I&#39;ve come across in a long time, and neatly executed as well.</p><br /><div>The classic Greek gods, Zeus, Apollo, Aphrodite, Eros, Artemis etc. are living in a rather dirty house in London, just about keeping up with their godly duties, though nobody believes in them anymore. A couple of mortals get mixed up in their petty bickering and things spiral from there. The way these classic gods and their legends are mixed in to modern day London is brilliantly entertaining, and the plot picks up speed and keeps it going. More than many books I&#39;ve read recently I struggled to put it down.</div><br /><div>It&#39;s not quite perfect - in some indefinable way it just seemed a little simplistic at times - but definitely comes highly recommended.</div>

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Beer Review: Wadworth 6X (can)
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: beer-review-wadworth-6x-can
CATEGORY: Beer
CATEGORY: Food and Drink

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2008/12/beer-review-wadworth-6x-can.html 
DATE: 12/04/2008 01:44:29 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>For once I strayed away from just slinging a four pack of <a href="/atc/2008/11/beer-review-greene-king-ipa-can.html" title="My review of Greene King IPA in a can">Greene King IPA</a> cans into the trolley and instead went for something markedly more expensive, in the interests of variety.</p><div>At 4.3% this has a midrange punch (but not too much for a weekday evening) and plenty of colour and flavour. It&#39;s got quite a malty, fruity flavour, which was almost edging into being over the top for me, for a daily evening beer at any rate. That said, probably better to have one of these than two of something more nondescript, and I&#39;m sure the doctor would agree! Recommended for most purposes, especially as we head into the ever darker and colder months.</div><br /><div style="text-align: center;"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e0158883401053637a0e9970c-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="Wadworth6X" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e0158883401053637a0e9970c " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e0158883401053637a0e9970c-400wi" style="width: 400px; " /></a>
 <br /></div>

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Scotch Pancakes / Drop Scones
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: scotch-pancakes-drop-scones
CATEGORY: Food and Drink

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2008/12/scotch-pancakes-drop-scones.html 
DATE: 12/03/2008 06:54:39 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>Apparently some people call Scotch pancakes drop scones instead. It&#39;s a strange world and takes all sorts, or so I&#39;m reliably informed.</p><div><br /><div>That aside, I decided to make some from scratch for breakfast a couple of weeks back, to go with the maple cured bacon and maple syrup we already had. We always used to just buy a packet of Scotch pancakes and stick them in the toaster, but we didn&#39;t have any in and that small problem wasn&#39;t going to stand in the way of my breakfast.</div><br /><div>The recipe&#39;s really ludicrously simple, though the wife seems to have hidden the Hugh Fearnley-Doodah book I used at the time. Luckily, I found <a href="http://www.guardian.co.uk/lifeandstyle/2006/oct/21/recipes.foodanddrink1" target="_blank">his recipe online here</a> and I think it&#39;s about the same as the one I used from the book. What confuses me though is the one from the book made about 30 scones so I halved the quantities, whereas this online version says it makes 12, but looks like the version that I read before halving, so use your own judgement :-) One thing I found is that weighing out really small quantities accurately is quite tricky with analog scales, but it didn&#39;t seem to cause a problem.</div><br /><div style="text-align: center;"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e01588834010536356668970c-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="ScotchPancakesBatter" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e01588834010536356668970c " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e01588834010536356668970c-300wi" style="width: 300px; " /></a>&#0160; <a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e0158883401053635669a970c-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="ScotchPancakesFrying" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e0158883401053635669a970c " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e0158883401053635669a970c-300wi" style="width: 300px; " /></a>
 <br /></div><br /><div>It&#39;s really very quick and easy to make the batter, the critical thing being the liquidity. I must have got it right, because they spread out nicely to just the right thickness on the hot frying pan and looked like the real deal. I found with a non-stick pan they were really trouble free when flipping, not requiring careful extra oiling as Hugh suggested. I was able to do four at a time, and stacked them up when done, but I failed to keep them warm enough whilst then frying the bacon (I wanted to use that same pan) so the butter didn&#39;t melt on them as well as I&#39;d have liked. Next time I&#39;ll probably keep them under foil and maybe give them a quick zap in the microwave just the steam them up a bit before bringing to the table.</div><br /><div>Finally - and frankly this was a touch of genius-like inspiration - I served with lime wedges. The lime juice cuts through the sweet maple syrup to take it to another level of breakfast heaven! Look at that picture and imagine the pancakes buttered and real Canadian maple syrup drizzled all over..</div><br /><div style="text-align: center;"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340105363566eb970c-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="ScotchPancakesPlated" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e015888340105363566eb970c " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340105363566eb970c-500wi" style="width: 500px; " /></a>
 <br /></div></div>

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: The Quest for the Perfect Flapjack
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: the-quest-for-the-perfect-flapjack
CATEGORY: Food and Drink

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2008/11/the-quest-for-the-perfect-flapjack.html 
DATE: 11/29/2008 06:30:52 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>I&#39;ve almost always been disappointed with bought flapjacks, or flapjacks made by other people - because I have a very particular vision in my mind of how the perfect flapjack should be, which is apparently different to everyone else&#39;s. To me, perfection is golden, sweet, initially slightly brittle yet yielding to become jaw-achingly chewy. The overriding flavour should be oats and golden syrup. Putting flour in a flapjack is anathema of course - this is a chewy, oaty treat, not a soft cake!</p><div>So I set out to create the perfect flapjack by starting with a basic recipe and modifying till I found nirvana in a baking tin. My first effort was just a straightforward attempt to act as a benchmark, using the following straightforward approach, modified from several I found across the internet:</div><br />

<ul>
<li><span style="font-style: italic;">125g Whole rolled jumbo oats</span></li>
<li><span style="font-style: italic;">125g Oatmeal (because all whole oats is apparently a bit much)</span></li>
<li><span style="font-style: italic;">150g butter</span></li>
<li><span style="font-style: italic;">75g Golden syrup (the single most important ingredient - Tate &amp; Lyle of course)</span></li>
<li><span style="font-style: italic;">75g caster sugar (I used golden caster sugar)</span></li>
</ul>
<p><span style="font-style: italic;">

Melt the butter, syrup and sugar together in a pan, add everything else, stir together than put into a 20*20cm tin lined with baking parchment. Put in oven at 175c for 20mins or so, but if you&#39;re oven&#39;s anything like mine you really need to keep an eye on it!</span></p><div><span style="font-style: italic;"><br /></span></div><div>Here are the before and after going in the oven shots:</div><br /><div style="text-align: center;"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e0158883401053622cb4c970b-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="FlapjackRaw" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e0158883401053622cb4c970b " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e0158883401053622cb4c970b-300wi" style="width: 300px; " /></a>
 <a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e0158883401053622cb19970b-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="FlapjackCooked" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e0158883401053622cb19970b " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e0158883401053622cb19970b-300wi" style="width: 300px; " /></a>
 <br /></div><div style="text-align: center;"><br /></div><div style="text-align: left;">Looked pretty good and tasted OK, with decent chewy texture, but not the flavour I was after - just not enough golden syrupyness coming through.</div><div style="text-align: left;"><br /></div><div style="text-align: left;">So I tried again, this time using much more syrup and much less butter (they were a bit greasy first time). I also threw in a handful of sultanas to add moist chewiness and flavour. After only 15 minutes it was &#39;done&#39; and came out looking like this:</div><div style="text-align: left;"><br /></div><div style="text-align: center;"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340105362b1f21970c-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="FlapjackBurnt" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e015888340105362b1f21970c " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340105362b1f21970c-400wi" style="width: 400px; " /></a>
 <br /></div><div style="text-align: center;"><br /></div><div style="text-align: left;">It took some serious effort to cut it into those few pieces, but I gave up after that. Those black blobs are the sultanas, embedded within the concrete that was the &#39;improved&#39; flapjack. Honestly you could have made houses with this stuff. I think I know what the butter&#39;s for now! The experiment will continue...</div>
-----

TITLE: Ouch: Hernia Repaired
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: ouch-hernia-repaired
CATEGORY: Me

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2008/11/ouch-hernia-repaired.html 
DATE: 11/28/2008 05:50:18 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>Just 48 hours ago I had a bilateral inguinal hernia repair, by way of open surgery (rather than laparoscopic &#39;keyhole&#39; surgery). Which is to say I was sliced open twice, either side of my lower abdomen, just above the groin. Plastic meshes were inserted to patch up the problem and stop it happening again. This is very routine surgery, but it was still rather traumatic and the recovery has not been a breeze. Still, I made it home within 24 hours and am getting slowly better now, though I&#39;m still very inflexible and pained. I don&#39;t know what I&#39;d have done without my wife to help me!</p><br /><div>I expect to be off work for another week, and maybe getting back to playing football within a couple of months. We&#39;ll see.</div><br /><div>If anyone has any specific questions about the routine, I&#39;d be happy to answer them as I found it really useful to have lots of first-hand information before I went into it.</div>

TITLE: Beer Review: Budweiser Budvar Dark

<p>No, the other Budweiser! The Czech one that makes good beers!</p><div>This dark variant of the much acclaimed Budvar apparently won Best Beer in the World or somesuch at a worldwide competion in 2007. AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Random Photo: Spurt - Sanssouci
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: random-photo-spurt---sanssouci
CATEGORY: Photography
CATEGORY: Travel

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2008/11/random-photo-spurt---sanssouci.html 
DATE: 11/09/2008 10:25:02 AM
-----
BODY:
<p>Another picture from the delightful gardens of Sanssouci near Potsdam in Germany. AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Lifts: Britain vs The Rest of the World
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: lifts-britain-vs-the-rest-of-the-world
CATEGORY: Design

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2008/11/lifts-britain-vs-the-rest-of-the-world.html 
DATE: 11/07/2008 10:32:57 PM
-----
BODY:
<div>Britain loses, which is why I&#39;d rather take the stairs.</div><br /><div><span style="font-weight: bold; font-size: 14px; font-family: &#39;Trebuchet MS&#39;; ">Britain</span></div><br /><div>In this country all lifts are programmed to sap the living souls of their occupants. You get into the lift and then wait an eternity, jabbing at the buttons in the forlorn hope that they might be connected to something. Eventually it realises it&#39;s a lift rather than a walk-in wardrobe and shuts the doors. Your captor now waits a while, pondering the endless infinity of space. Some time later, maybe a week, maybe a month, the slow voyage begins. I hope you brought a packed lunch, we&#39;re going three floors here! Just us your pension matures you arrive a few tens of feet higher than you started when you were a sprightly young thing. But let us rest a while, there&#39;s no hurry! Why open the doors immediately when there are so many fun things to do in the lift? The grim reaper circles as the sands of time run out and finally the lift lets you go back out into the world. Then it sits there with its mouth open, like the &#39;special&#39; kid at school, if only you could remember that far back.<br /></div><br /><div><span style="font-weight: bold; font-size: 14px; font-family: &#39;Trebuchet MS&#39;; ">The Rest of the World</span></div><br /><div>Press button in lobby - the doors open a fraction of a second before you thought you touched the button. Step inside and the doors close, patting you on the bottom as you enter. In the time it takes you to turn around, you&#39;ve arrived at your destination floor, simply by thinking about where you want it to take you. The doors open whilst the lift is still moving and your foot hits the carpet outside at the exact same moment that the lift stops. Your face creases into a grimace as you think back to Blighty and wonder why Messrs Otis and Schindler send us the factory seconds.</div><br /><div>But seriously, why are lifts in the UK so utterly terrible?</div><br />

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Book Review: I Believe in Yesterday  - Tim Moore
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: book-review-i-believe-in-yesterday---tim-moore
CATEGORY: Books
CATEGORY: Culture

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2008/11/book-review-i-believe-in-yesterday---tim-moore.html 
DATE: 11/05/2008 09:12:09 PM
-----
BODY:
<iframe frameborder="0" marginheight="0" marginwidth="0" scrolling="no" src="http://rcm-uk.amazon.co.uk/e/cm?t=alwthecri-21&amp;o=2&amp;p=8&amp;l=as1&amp;asins=0224077813&amp;fc1=000000&amp;IS2=1&amp;lt1=_blank&amp;m=amazon&amp;lc1=0000FF&amp;bc1=000000&amp;bg1=FFFFFF&amp;f=ifr&amp;npa=1" style="float:right;margin-left:15px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:10px;width:120px;height:240px;"></iframe>

<p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica">I&#39;m a big fan of Tim Moore&#39;s books, and the &quot;do some wacky stuff then write about it in an amusing way&quot; genre as a whole. That said, his previous effort Nul Points, about the history and characters of the Eurovision Song Contest left me cold - in fact I never even finished it. So I was a little nervous about this very latest tome, which has a similar historical bent, rather than a completely asinine caper at its core&#0160; (like pilgramiging through Spain with a donkey - quite an ass-inine caper). I needn&#39;t have worried.</p>
<p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica; min-height: 14.0px"></p>


<p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica">The world of living history (historical re-enactment is perhaps a more meaningful term to most) turns out to be a rich seam ripe for comedy mining. Certainly more so than going to visit a Norwegian who once sang on tele. Fighting as part of a Roman garrison against the Gauls, living the life of a Tudor chamberlain and a succession of other historical roles present a cavalcade of hilarity, mostly sourced from the usually very committed people involved and his own struggles to fit in and be authentic. There are some truly laugh out loud moments and the book is fairly un-put-downable.</p>
<p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica; min-height: 14.0px"></p>
<p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica">Will you learn a great deal about history by reading this book? Probably not, but you&#39;ll learn a lot about historical re-enactment. I was really surprised by some of it, especially the authenticity of the violence! Tim was too, clearly.</p>
<p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica; min-height: 14.0px"></p>
<p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica">Final verdict: A cracking example of the genre and highly recommended. I hope the next one is as good.</p><p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica"></p><p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; margin-bottom:25px; font: 12.0px Helvetica">Here are my favourite other books of his:</p><p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica"></p>

<center>
<iframe frameborder="0" marginheight="0" marginwidth="0" scrolling="no" src="http://rcm-uk.amazon.co.uk/e/cm?t=alwthecri-21&amp;o=2&amp;p=8&amp;l=as1&amp;asins=0099433826&amp;fc1=000000&amp;IS2=1&amp;lt1=_blank&amp;m=amazon&amp;lc1=0000FF&amp;bc1=000000&amp;bg1=FFFFFF&amp;f=ifr" style="width:120px;height:240px;"></iframe>&#0160;&#0160; &#0160; &#0160;

TITLE: Beer Review: Greene King IPA (Can)
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: beer-review-greene-king-ipa-can
CATEGORY: Beer
CATEGORY: Food and Drink

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2008/11/beer-review-greene-king-ipa-can.html 
DATE: 11/02/2008 04:53:40 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>This is a much maligned beer, with many beer snobs writing it off almost immediately for being weak (3.6%), in a can and from such a mainstream brewery. That said, this same beer (on draft) was champion beer of Britain (Bitter category) and silver overall in 2004. Some people were so horrified by this that they threw their CAMRA cards out of their prams at the time. Personally I rather like it!</p><div><br /><div>It&#39;s the four pack of cans that I reach for most often from the supermarket shelf, precisely because it&#39;s weak (I&#39;m a Radio 2 listening 30 year old now) and fairly cheap, whilst not being too bland or too over the top. You don&#39;t always want an intensely flavoured, knock your head off brew. It has a decent, malty flavour with a drinkable level of bitterness that&#39;s great when you&#39;re after a mild but satisfying beverage, and it doesn&#39;t too badly for having come in a can.</div><br /><div style="text-align: center;"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e01588834010535cc3684970b-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="GreeneKingIPA" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e01588834010535cc3684970b " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e01588834010535cc3684970b-400wi" style="width: 400px; " /></a>

<p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica">We went to meet some friends for lunch and a wander at <a href="http://www.waddesdon.org.uk/" target="_blank">Waddesdon Manor</a>, a National Trust property near Aylesbury, about halfway between us in St Albans and them in Birmingham. We&#39;re all NT members so it&#39;s completely free to park and get in!</p>
<p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica; min-height: 14.0px"></p><p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica; min-height: 14.0px"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e01588834010535b90e0b970b-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="WaddesdonManor" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e01588834010535b90e0b970b " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e01588834010535b90e0b970b-400wi" style="width: 400px; " /></a>

<p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica">It&#39;s a bit of a strange place in that it&#39;s one of the most opulent and well looked after NT houses I&#39;ve been to. Perhaps there is some private money in play too - courtesy of the Rothschild&#39;s - that web link above is not a National Trust website, though they have their <a href="http://www.nationaltrust.org.uk/main/w-waddesdonmanor" target="_blank">own page on the place</a> as well. Strange.</p><p><a href="http://www.nationaltrust.org.uk/main/w-waddesdonmanor"></a></p><p><a href="http://www.nationaltrust.org.uk/main/w-waddesdonmanor"></a></p><p><a href="http://www.nationaltrust.org.uk/main/w-waddesdonmanor"><p></p>

</a></p><p></p><p></p><p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica"><a href="http://www.nationaltrust.org.uk/main/w-waddesdonmanor"><span style="font-family: &#39;Trebuchet MS&#39;; font-size: 13px; line-height: 15px; "></span></a><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e01588834010535bff85f970c-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="float: right;"><img alt="WaddesdonRushes" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e01588834010535bff85f970c selected " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e01588834010535bff85f970c-250wi" style="width: 250px; margin: 0px 0px 5px 5px;" /></a>

</p><p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica"></p><p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica">We didn&#39;t explore that much of it this time (we&#39;ve been there once before) since we had our friends&#39; giggling young one in tow. But we did see the front garden (driveway, grass, trees, sadly dry fountain) and the back (mountainous flower-beds and pleasant water features overlooking distant countryside - see pictures) and the inside (no photos allowed) and the Stables for lunch.</p>
<p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica; min-height: 14.0px"></p><p><span style="font-size: 12px; font-family: Helvetica; ">

 Last time we visited, we ate in the fancy kitchen restaurant and I had the most wonderful duck ever, along with a cracking glass of red. This time we went for the family option in the Stables restaurant and though the service was a bit slipshod and the glasses dirty, the food was really surprisingly good.</span></p><p></p>

TITLE: Beer Review: Nils Oscar God Lager
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: 0
ALLOW PINGS: 1

CATEGORY: Beer
CATEGORY: Food and Drink

DATE: 10/24/2008 08:58:06 PM

BODY:
<p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica">Right from the start I'll point out that God Lager is Swedish for good lager, though the rear label makes plenty of hints that this is in fact a divine beverage. I bought it from Waitrose purely because it looked a little unorthodox on the shelf and seemed to promise something that it could surely never live up to.</p>
<p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica; min-height: 14.0px"></p>
<p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica">And frankly it didn't. This is a fairly straightforward lager in pretty much every sense, though it has a very fine bubble (in fact it almost seemed flat) that gives it a somewhat classy feel, but only just. Maybe it only achieves perfection in being the perfect example of average, unassuming lager? Even if it is, I need something with a bit more flavour to get excited about. Still - credit to the Nils Oscar Company's marketing department for a good gimmick.</p><p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica"></p><p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica"></p><p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica"></p><p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica"></p><p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica"><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e01588834010535bb7a04970c-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, '_blank', 'width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0' ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img  alt="GodLager" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e01588834010535bb7a04970c " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e01588834010535bb7a04970c-500wi" style="width: 500px; margin-top:15px;"></a>

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Whipsnade Zoo
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: whipsnade-zoo

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2008/10/whipsnade-zoo.html 
DATE: 10/21/2008 09:46:36 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>We went to Whipsnade Zoo at the weekend, because it&#39;s fairly close by (surprisingly so - only took 25 mins from St Albans) and we&#39;ve been meaning to for a while. A two-for-one voucher from a cereal box was the clincher, saving us £17 on the entry price. We did exactly the same for London Zoo a couple of months back. With Whipsnade being run by ZSL it&#39;s a sort of outpost of London Zoo and so we couldn&#39;t help but compare and contrast the two.</p><br /><div>The first thing we noticed is that it&#39;s a lot colder, windier and greyer. But that could just have been autumn arriving with full force. It&#39;s certainly a lot more open, with some really huge paddocks of green grass, trees, hummocks etc. with animals dotted about within them, almost Safari park like. That does mean there&#39;s less variety overall and it&#39;s a bit of a walk to get around, but it&#39;s pleasant and you feel the animals are probably happier with the extra space. At least some of them. One medium sized oak was home to this delightful red panda. It was easily the cutest thing we saw all day, beating the otters into second place.</div><br /><div><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e01588834010535a11f73970c-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="RedPanda" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e01588834010535a11f73970c " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e01588834010535a11f73970c-400wi" style="width: 400px; " /></a>
 <br /></div><br /><div>It struck me that all it had to do to escape was walk to the end of a branch and jump past the fence. Presumably it isn&#39;t so inclined. I always seem to end up figuring out escape plans for the animals, and it often looks like it wouldn&#39;t be so hard. If the chimpanzees simply got together and dragged a branch into the right place they could be up and over the fence, tall as it is, in a jiffy.</div><br /><div>We caught a sealion show, which was quite impressive. Three out of the four of them provided accomplished routines, whilst the fourth (Dominic, the youngest) played the fool, which added to the charm.</div><br /><div><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e01588834010535a123c9970c-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="SealionsGroup" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e01588834010535a123c9970c " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e01588834010535a123c9970c-400wi" style="width: 400px; " /></a>
 <br /></div><br /><div>I took my big Nikon 80-400mm VR lens and was glad I did as it really helped to get in close, especially given the large enclosures often meant the animals were far away. It&#39;s not that great for action, being a bit slow, but I got a half-reasonable jumping sealion.</div><br /><div><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e01588834010535a125e9970c-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="SealionJump" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e01588834010535a125e9970c " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e01588834010535a125e9970c-400wi" style="width: 400px; " /></a>
 <br /></div><br /><div>I rate the zoo quite highly and would recommend allocating a whole day to visit, though it&#39;s a shame it doesn&#39;t have a bit more dense indoor stuff (insects, reptiles, fish etc.) to counter-balance the wide-open spaces. It has just the one very cramped Discovery Centre which is decent, if a bit MDF heavy, but the zoo could do with more of the same, spread about the place and implemented in a slicker fashion. There&#39;s a bit of a crumbling feel in a few places and the signage to tell you what you&#39;re looking at is woeful for most of the outdoor stuff.</div><br /><div>I took a great many pictures, as usual, but I&#39;ll finish with an obligatory tiger - grrrrr!</div><br /><div><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340105359a054a970b-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="TigerSleepy (1)" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e015888340105359a054a970b " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340105359a054a970b-400wi" style="width: 400px; " /></a>
 <br /></div>

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Book Review: Hugh Fearlessly Eats It All
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: 0
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: book-review-hugh-fearlessly-eats-it-all
CATEGORY: Books
CATEGORY: Food and Drink

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2008/10/book-review-hugh-fearlessly-eats-it-all.html 
DATE: 10/15/2008 10:36:27 PM
-----
BODY:
<p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica">I picked up a paperback copy of this book from the River Cottage open day a couple of months back. We queued for a good long while to get my wife's big new Hugh cookery book signed, but I didn't trouble him with my less significant purchase. I later discovered that it was signed inside the front cover anyway. Obviously he was taking no chances!</p>
<p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica; min-height: 14.0px"></p>
<iframe src="http://rcm-uk.amazon.co.uk/e/cm?t=alwthecri-21&o=2&p=8&l=as1&asins=0747589259&fc1=000000&IS2=1&lt1=_blank&m=amazon&lc1=0000FF&bc1=000000&bg1=FFFFFF&f=ifr" style="float:right;width:120px;height:240px;margin-left:10px; margin-bottom:10px;" scrolling="no" marginwidth="0" marginheight="0" frameborder="0"></iframe>

<p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica">I also discovered that it wasn't quite what I thought it was. Not for the first time, I had failed to notice that this is a collection of previous scribblings by the floppy haired foodie, from various Sunday supplements and trendy lifestyle magazines. Jeremy Clarkson pulled the same trick on me a couple of years back. Thing is, they don't go out of their way to make it clear just what you're buying, choosing the words on the cover oh so cleverly, to be accurate but not quite clue you in if you didn't already know. I find this ironic since a lot of the book consists of Hugh pouring forth with righteous indignation about all the commercial dishonesty out there in the food business.</p>
<p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica; min-height: 14.0px"></p>
<p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica">The first chapter is actually a bit wearing as Hugh lays it on extremely thick, making and re-making the same simple points over and over again about McDonalds and their ilk. It got a bit tiresome and I very nearly gave up entirely. However I persevered and it got better from there on, though the whole volume is still preachy and sometimes patronising. That said, yesterday I bought Waitrose' organic cheddar even though it was 10p per kilo more expensive that the normal stuff,  which is no doubt made out of cigarette butts and arsenic, with old AA membership cards ground up and added for colour. Actually I bet it's exactly the same bar the packaging. So Hugh's taught me two things there: to search out decent ingredients with good provenance; and to maintain an unhealthy level of cynicism and suspicion at all times.</p>
<p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica; min-height: 14.0px"></p>
<p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica">Overall it's a good book that I'd recommend for anyone that likes Hugh to start with and just likes good food writing. The best bits of the book are the gastronomic exotica that the cover promises and Hugh's excellent style, full of wit and anecdote and very giving of himself. He does go on about brains a lot though.</p>
-----

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Wembley: England 5 - 1 Kazakhstan
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: wembley-england-5---1-kazakhstan
CATEGORY: Beer
CATEGORY: Sports
CATEGORY: Travel

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2008/10/wembley-england-5---1-kazakhstan.html 
DATE: 10/12/2008 04:40:06 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>The missus had the brilliant idea of going to see England play at Wembley, so we did just that yesterday! It&#39;s quite a slick operation, as you&#39;d hope, with the tube and the venue doing an impressive job of getting 90,000 fans to and from the game. In fact the Jubilee line tube we left on was only half-full as the old bridges at the station just can&#39;t deliver people to the platform fast enough. Still, it only took about 30 mins to get from our seat into a tube.</p><div>I was shocked and I suppose only mildly amazed that there was no beer for sale in the venue. I&#39;d assumed that you wouldn&#39;t be allowed it in the bowl itself, but that it would be available in the concourses. And yes, there were the signs, proudly proclaiming &quot;Pie and a pint&quot;, &quot;Cold Beer here&quot; etc. But when I asked I was laughed at. I did later spot a small sign saying that UEFA had decreed that this is the way it must be, but it&#39;s just harsh to advertise beer everywhere whilst not serving any. The tickets and FA website didn&#39;t make any mention of it either, that I could see. How very uncivilised.</div><p><br /><span style="color: #0000ff; "><img alt="Wembley" border="0" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e0158883401053579f748970b selected " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e0158883401053579f748970b-800wi" style="cursor: pointer !important; border-top-style: none; border-right-style: none; border-bottom-style: none; border-left-style: none; border-width: initial; border-color: initial; float: right; padding-left:15px;" title="Wembley" /></span></p><div>That said, it was the least hostile atmosphere I&#39;ve ever known at a football game, and the lack of beer is probably to thank for that. At no point did I even fear for my life! How very civilised.</div><br /><div>The ticket made it VERY clear that cameras were strictly verboten, so with a heavy heart we didn&#39;t take any, which is shame because the new stadium is a fine photographic muse. That&#39;s why you have to do with a poor snap from my phone as we sat behind the goal. England scored all 5 into that goal in the second half, and the England Band (sponsored by Pukka Pies apparently) played about ten rows behind us. And in front of us sat a woman with a massive camera. In fact we appeared to be about the only people there without one. That&#39;s what you get for playing by the rules.</div>
-----

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Review: Astronaut Ice Cream
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: review-astronaut-ice-cream
CATEGORY: Food and Drink
CATEGORY: Science

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2008/10/review-astronaut-ice-cream.html 
DATE: 10/09/2008 08:53:47 PM
-----
BODY:
<p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica; min-height: 14.0px">A recently hectic calendar has meant no time to go to the supermarket, which isn&#39;t such a bad thing as it has shown us the back of our kitchen cupboards for the first time in a while. As we chomp through the ancient stocks a few surprises have come to light. One such was Astronaut Ice Cream, given to me as a Xmas present a year or two ago, but still good till December 2010 if you believe the foil sachet. And yes, this was in the cupboard, not the freezer.</p>
<p style="text-align: center;margin-top: 0px; margin-right: 0px; margin-bottom: 0px; margin-left: 0px; font: normal normal normal 12px/normal Helvetica; min-height: 14px; "></p>
<p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica">It&#39;s real ice cream, but freeze dried, so all the water has been removed. I expected to find a powder to which I&#39;d add water for some surreally room temperature ice creamy experience, but no. Inside the feather light pack (contents: 19g) is a single slice of Neapolitan ice cream. It looks like ice cream, but it&#39;s completely dry and crisp, with the texture of a really fine, dense foam. And apparently it&#39;s &quot;ready to eat&quot; as is.</p><p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica"></p><p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica"></p><p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica"></p>
<p style="text-align: center;margin-top: 0px; margin-right: 0px; margin-bottom: 0px; margin-left: 0px; font: normal normal normal 12px/normal Helvetica; min-height: 14px; "><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340105356dafd8970b-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false" style="display: inline;"><img alt="AstronautIceCream" class="at-xid-6a00e5550e015888340105356dafd8970b " src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.a/6a00e5550e015888340105356dafd8970b-320wi" /></a>
 </p><p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica; min-height: 14.0px"></p>
<p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica">So I snapped off a piece (actually the block was somewhat shattered to start with) trying not to get shards of ice cream in my eye and popped it in my mouth. It&#39;s crunchy to start with, but very quickly turns to dust which immediately combines with the saliva in your mouth to become something like ice cream. However the airy texture has been lost and there&#39;s only so much saliva in your mouth, so it&#39;s denser and perhaps pastier than the real thing. That said, it tastes the part - no doubt about it. I wonder if freezing the block to start with would add to the ice-creamy experience or just make it weirder.</p>
<p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica; min-height: 14.0px"></p>
<p style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px 0.0px; font: 12.0px Helvetica">I can see how the weight saving and longevity of freeze-drying are handy for trips into space, but the astronaut will still need to consume the same total quantity of water so I would have thought that vacuum packed hydrated food would take up less space overall and just be outright nicer. In fact paraphrasing from <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freeze-dried_ice_cream" target="_blank" title="Wikipedia article on space ice cream">Wikipedia&#39;s article</a> although freeze-dried ice cream was developed on request, it wasn&#39;t that popular, and was only taken into space once on Apollo 7 in 1968.&quot;&#0160;It was a good present though and a conversation starter.</p>

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Accordions: The Parrot Has Landed!
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: markdown
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: accordions-the
CATEGORY: Music

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2008/10/accordions-the.html 
DATE: 10/01/2008 08:44:21 AM
-----
BODY:
<p>Read the <a href="/atc/2008/09/accordions-ever.html">first</a> and <a href="/atc/2008/09/accordions-firs.html">second</a> instalments if you haven't already.</p>

<p>With a renewed vigour I set out in search of a larger selection of accordions, courtesy of a dedicated shop stacked ceiling to floor with them: <a href="http://www.accordionsoflondon.com/index.php">Accordions of London</a> in Kilburn. The proprietor, John Leslie, is a fantastic player (he treated me to a bit of a show piece), teacher and all round accordion authority. At least that's the way it seemed and I have no reason to doubt it!</p>

<p>I learnt yet more interesting things (as I am prone to doing):</p>

<ul>
<li><p>His Chinese accordions are similarly priced and look near identical to the ones I saw the day before, though John says his are better as he's very particular with the factory about exactly how they are specced. They certainly seemed a bit nicer to play, but I'm so far from being the authority on such subtleties that I'd have to place an expensive long distance phone call in order to speak to that authority.</p></li>
<li><p>His Eastern European Luciano accordions are a bit more differentiated and I understand they come from the Weltmeister factory, but again, specced to John's exacting standards. The problem for me is that a half-decent size one of these starts at about £1000.</p></li>
<li><p>I had a go on one of the properly expensive machines (one of John's own) and it certainly felt nice and played beautifully. One thing I noted was that the more expensive the machine, the better it was at evenly putting out sound in both bass and treble at the same time. The ones I tried yesterday were terrible in that respect.</p></li>
<li><p>A proper non-budget model starts at about £1200 and that's second hand. One of the two rooms was filled with more serious models, ranging into the many thousands of pounds. And very nice (and heavy) I'm sure they were too!</p></li>
<li><p>John reckoned I should get a full size model (41 keys, 120 bass) because otherwise it wouldn't fit me properly. He advocates sitting down to play with the accordion well wedged between legs and chin. Smaller models can't be wedged in that manner.</p></li>
</ul>

<p>So, all very exciting, but it was looking like a bleak prospect for me and my limited budget. It was either that or pay £1200 for a fairly good 120 bass model, but I just couldn't bring myself to do that.</p>

<p>John and his assistant scoured the somewhat dusty shelves and eventually found a Parrot accordion for about half that price, with the full complement of keys and buttons, 4 treble voices with 13 switches and 5 bass voices with 6 switches. And a decent pair of straps and a hard case. So, the right size and well specced! It's a new accordion but it's been sat on the shelf for a few years, by a Chinese manufacturer of not particularly special repute. It's clearly not as good as most of the others in the shop, but it's now mine!</p>

<p>I'd post a photo, but I'm not picking it up until later in the week after the metal strap bracket has been moved so as not to dig into my leg. All that remains now is to lug it home and learn how to play the darn thing.</p>

-----

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Accordions: First Contact
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: markdown
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: accordions-firs
CATEGORY: Music

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2008/09/accordions-firs.html 
DATE: 09/30/2008 06:15:24 PM
-----
BODY:
<p><a href="/atc/2008/09/accordions-ever.html">Read the first instalment</a> if you haven't already.</p>

<p>The thot plickens! I have now visited a genuine purveyor of accordions: <a href="http://www.hobgoblin.com/london/index.php">Hobgoblin Music in London</a> - on Rathbone Place just between Goodge Street and Tottenham Court Road. It's a cracking little shop, rammed full of instrumental exotica. I struggled to pull my gaze away from the extensive selection of tasty banjos, but a helpful assistant saddled me up with a weighty accordion and off I went.</p>

<p>I didn't go far though, managing only to randomly jab keys and buttons in a tuneless mêlée of fumbling fingers. I learnt some useful things:</p>

<ul>
<li><p>The left hand is incapable of reaching even the limited 72 buttons on my test model, without resetting the hand position within the strap. That strap has to be quite tight to stop your hand sliding up to the top due to the effect of gravity on that end of the machine.</p></li>
<li><p>The tighter the hand strap, the less gravity is a problem but the less freedom you have to move, even though the only way you can move is upwards - due to that pesky gravity.</p></li>
<li><p>You can't see that huge field of identical buttons under the fingers of your left hand, so all you've got to go on is feel. One of the buttons has a concave top to differentiate it from the others, and presumably everything else is relative. Einstein himself would struggle to find that one dimpled button in the first place, let alone suss out the others. Figure out those buttons and you've figured out the accordion I reckon.</p></li>
<li><p>If you don't squeeze hard enough on the bellows, you don't get any sound at all from the piano side. All the air rushes out of the bass reeds instead, given there are more of them open and they're bigger. It stands to reason, but the more notes you play at once (including chord buttons, or using multiple reed banks) the more air you need to keep it all going.</p></li>
<li><p>The bellows trap your t-shirt when compressed. Remember to free yourself when unstrapping.</p></li>
<li><p>Even for £900 you just get a smallish, plasticky accordion, albeit a Czech one. You'll pay about £350 for the Chinese equivalent, which seemed largely identical in most respects, but had almost no feedback from the buttons used to select treble reed banks.</p></li>
</ul>

<p>I decided not to buy right there and then. I think I need to see a larger selection and maybe some second hand instruments to find what I'm after. Quality is important to me, but it's going to be difficult to find that elusive feel of solid craftsmanship for the cash I have to splash. I'll report back on the quest.</p>

--------
AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Accordions: Everything I Need to Know, Condensed
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: markdown
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: accordions-ever

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2008/09/accordions-ever.html 
DATE: 09/29/2008 09:51:41 AM
-----
BODY:
<p>I've been looking to buy a piano accordion. Why? I just love the sound, they're an intriguing and mysterious instrument to most people and I have a growing habit of buying interesting instruments then failing to learn to play them. Still, a lot of the fun is in the chase, and I'm maximising my enjoyment of this one!</p>

<p>To that end, I've been devouring information about piano accordions online, though I'm still yet to actually touch one! Hopefully I'll manage that later this week with a visit to a London music shop, but for now, here's my ultra-condensed guide to what I think I need to know about accordions in order to make an informed purchasing decision. We'll see if I was actually right.</p>

<ul>
<li><p>Piano accordions can have different numbers of piano keys (right-hand) and bass buttons (left-hand). The 'full' set is 41 piano keys and 120 bass buttons.</p></li>
<li><p>The bass buttons (in a 120 bass at least) are laid out in 6 rows, with top two rows being single note counter-bass and bass, the the remaining four playing chords rooted on their associated bass note. So the left hand can play individual notes and chords. This is known as a Stradella bass system.</p></li>
<li><p>A free bass system just has lots of individual notes, so you must form chords manually with multiple presses at once. This is considered by some to be a more purist approach and allows greater musical flexibility, especially for the classical scene.</p></li>
<li><p>Some 'converter' accordions can switch between Stradella and free bass. I'd like one of those (I want the moon on a stick) but I get the impression they're not so common and probably not cheap.</p></li>
<li><p>Speaking of cheap, though you can get small accordions (e.g. with only as few as eight bass buttons) for less than £100, it looks like you need to spend £400 or more to get a 120 bass accordion from a cheap Chinese manufacturer. £1500 will buy a half-decent Italian model, but the options just get more expensive from there.</p></li>
<li><p>Accordions are heavy - think 8Kg or more. They come with shoulder straps as a rule.</p></li>
<li><p>There is more than one way to tune an accordion, giving quite different types of sound. Tuning is a job for an expert (requires tweaking metal reeds) and probably done every five years or more, so best buy one that's tuned well to start with!</p></li>
<li><p>It doesn't matter how hard you press the piano keys or buttons - volume is controlled by your pressure on the bellows. Apparently this can be hard for a pianist to get to grips with, being more akin to bowing a cello.</p></li>
</ul>

<p>I repeat: this is just what I think is true - I stand to be corrected, and will post an update as the story unfolds.</p>

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Beer Review: Sharp's Honey Spice Wheat Beer
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: markdown
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: beer-review-sha
CATEGORY: Beer
CATEGORY: Food and Drink

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2008/09/beer-review-sha.html 
DATE: 09/27/2008 03:14:34 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>I spotted this beer at a pound a bottle in Sainsbury's so grabbed a couple as it sounded really different. It describes itself as being made with wheat and barley malts (rather than just barley as is normal), fermented with honey then conditioned for six months with spices - though it doesn't say which spices!</p>

<p><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/photos/uncategorized/2008/09/27/sharpsbeer.jpg"><img alt="Sharpsbeer" title="Sharpsbeer" src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/images/2008/09/27/sharpsbeer.jpg" width="350" height="237" border="0"  /></a></p>

<p>I thought it might be similar to a continental wheat beer - cloudy white with hints of spice - but it's definitely its own style of beer. It's a very rich amber and almost entirely clear. The flavour is quite deep, bitter and smoky with a slightly burnt malt flavour reminiscent of a stout. The spice just leaves a subtle, lingering flavour in the mouth.</p>

<p>At 6% ABV and with a real depth of colour and flavour it's not a 'light' beer in any sense. It's almost a winter warmer, but I hadn't twigged that until I'd poured it to accompany the grand prix qualifying mid-afternoon. Still, I quite like it and it was well priced, even for a 330ml bottle, so cheers!</p>

AUTHOR: Sam Carr
TITLE: Kew Gardens, featuring Rhizotron and Xstrata Treetop Walkway!
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: markdown
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: kew-gardens-fea
CATEGORY: Nature
CATEGORY: Travel

UNIQUE URL: http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/2008/09/kew-gardens-fea.html 
DATE: 09/23/2008 10:06:38 PM
-----
BODY:
<p><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.shared/image.html?/photos/uncategorized/2008/09/23/kewbiglilies_2.jpg" onclick="window.open(this.href, '_blank', 'width=678,height=1024,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0'); return false"><img alt="Kewbiglilies_2" title="Kewbiglilies_2" src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/images/2008/09/23/kewbiglilies_2.jpg" width="200" height="302" border="0" style="float: right; margin: 0px 0px 5px 5px;" /></a>
Almost every weekend this summer a trip to Kew Gardens has been on the cards, and finally we made it happen. We managed to pick a great day for it too - even wearing sunscreen for only about the second time this year. Having heard so much about the wonders of Kew we were really looking forward to it, but could it possibly live up to our expectations?</p>

<h2>Getting There</h2>

<p>Round the M25 and in on the M4 was easy enough but the signage ran out just when we got close and we spent twenty minutes trying to find the official parking. The pay and display machines in the long, slender car park mischievously require £5 in change, which means a long walk to the main ticket booth and back to the car, then back to the booth to actually enter the gardens if you're unlucky. Nice.</p>

<h2>And We're In!</h2>

<p>Once in, I had to reset my expectations a bit. The gardens consist mostly of flat lawns with trees and bushes and buildings scattered about. Not to mention so much goose poo that it was a struggle to sit down and eat our sandwiches. Ultimately it's more of a park than a garden. I'd expected clever planting to supply riots of colourful flowers even at the tail end of a bad summer but the palette is mostly green and brown throughout . I'd also expected meticulous and dense themed gardens like those at Butchart, which overwhelm the senses with their majesty and detail, each turn revealing endless new delights. But all I found was a couple of rather weak attempts at Alpine and Japanese gardens. I think Kew is hampered by its topology - being on the banks of the Thames it's pretty much entirely flat and there's little artificial landscaping to make it more interesting.</p>

<div style="clear:both"></div>

<p><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.shared/image.html?/photos/uncategorized/2008/09/23/kewpagoda.jpg" onclick="window.open(this.href, '_blank', 'width=678,height=1024,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0'); return false"><img alt="Kewpagoda" title="Kewpagoda" src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/images/2008/09/23/kewpagoda.jpg" width="200" height="302" border="0" style="float: left; margin: 0px 5px 5px 0px;" /></a></p>

<h2>Glass Houses</h2>

<p>It's just a whole different type of gardens to those that burst with exaggerated splendour from every angle. The best of the plants are kept indoors, under the panes of the still impressively huge old glasshouses. That said, they could do with a lick of paint - there's a whiff of fading grandeur about them and it'd be a shame to see them gradually crumble away for lack of funds or effort. The hot and sweaty palm house and its temperate brother were nice, but lacking a certain something. I've certainly seen better, or maybe I've been spoiled elsewhere. The modern Princess Diana building is huge and has some quality sections (who doesn't like a massive cactus) but you'll have to put the effort in to see it all as the path endlessly diverges and there are several ways in and out. I'd much prefer a single path that leads me neatly through everything there is to see, but then I'm a simple sort. It was more than a little surprising to see a large iguana basking at the edge of the water-lily pond, apparently free to come and go as it pleased with no staff anywhere to be seen. Strange.</p>

<h2>And Now, Your Main Feature...</h2>

<p>I understand that the ten storey pagoda used to be a major feature and it looks striking from a distance, but up close it's really very plain and peeling badly. The new hotness at Kew is the treetop walkway and its small underground atrium, or the "Rhizotron and Xstrata Treetop walkway" to use the proper and more than slightly over the top names. This is the new roller coaster in the theme park that is Kew Gardens, but the only sweat I broke was climbing the stairs. There is a lift, but it's exclusively for the disabled. Except it was broken so they were sat at the bottom not knowing what they were missing. Lucky them.</p>

<p>I've never known something so expensive and so hyped to be so disappointingly dull. [Insert your own gag about the Millennium Dome here, but I never went.] The implementation is clinical but boring - all bare concrete and rusting, sorry 'weathered' steel. You climb the stairs, you walk the loop, looking at some sweet chestnut branches relatively close up and you come back down again. The only information up there is presented via small sculptural metal plaques that convey only about ten words each. Perhaps they didn't want people to stop for long, so they can shepherd everyone through at speed and keep throughput up.</p>

<p>The only point of interest I remember from being up there was that it wobbled more than it looked like it should and the thin flooring flexed worryingly underfoot. In fact I'd stay a good distance away from any 40 stone leviathans that you might encounter up there (might being the operative word - it's a long way up the staircase) lest the whole thing give way. I'm sure it's structurally sound really, but if the majority of my interest is occupied by the feeling of uncertainty beneath my shoes then the whole expensive installation is a bit of a failure.</p>

<div style="clear:both"></div>

<p><a href="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/.shared/image.html?/photos/uncategorized/2008/09/23/kewiguana.jpg" onclick="window.open(this.href, '_blank', 'width=800,height=981,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0'); return false"><img alt="Kewiguana" title="Kewiguana" src="http://alwaysthecritic.typepad.com/atc/images/2008/09/23/kewiguana.jpg" width="200" height="245" border="0" style="float: right; margin: 0px 5px 5px 0px;" /></a></p>

<h2>In Summary</h2>

<p>Don't get me wrong, I've griped endlessly here but I had a great day out and I'm glad I went. It's just that it wasn't what I expected and many of the star attractions fell frustratingly short of where they could and should have been. The place is huge and we saw a vast number of different things - many of them quite good, but very few excellent. I'd recommend it, but I'd want to set your expectations first.</p>

-----
